label           = {{flatlist|\n* [[Panacea Records|Panacea]]\n* [[Big Loud]]\n* [[Republic Records|Republic]]\n* [[Mercury Records|Mercury]]\n}}\n}}\n}}\n\n'''Morgan Cole Wallen''' (born May 13, 1993) is an American [[country pop]] singer. He competed in the [[The Voice (American season 6)|sixth season of ''The Voice'']], originally as a member of [[Usher (musician)|Usher]]'s team, but later as a member of [[Adam Levine]]'s team. After being eliminated in the playoffs of that season, he signed to [[Panacea Records]], releasing his debut EP, ''[[Stand Alone (EP)|Stand Alone]]'', in 2015.\n\nIn 2016, Wallen signed to [[Big Loud]], releasing his debut album, ''[[If I Know Me (album)|If I Know Me]]'', in 2018.<ref>{{Cite web| date=2016-08-15| title=Big Loud Records Adds Morgan Wallen to Roster| publisher=Big Loud Records| url=https://bigloudrecords.com/big-loud-records-adds-morgan-wallen-to-roster/| access-date=2021-02-28| language=en-US| archive-date=January 18, 2022| archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220118182937/https://bigloudrecords.com/big-loud-records-adds-morgan-wallen-to-roster/| url-status=dead}}</ref> The album includes the singles \"[[Up Down (Morgan Wallen song)|Up Down]]\" (featuring [[Florida Georgia Line]]), \"[[Whiskey Glasses]]\", and \"[[Chasin' You]]\". ''If I Know Me'' reached No. 1 on the [[Top Country Albums|''Billboard'' Top Country Albums]] chart.<ref>{{Cite web|last=KFDI Staff|date=August 13, 2020|title=Morgan Wallen's 'If I Know Me' Reaches No. 1 on Billboard Top Country Albums Chart| url= https://www.kfdi.com/2020/08/13/morgan-wallens-if-i-know-me-reaches-no-1-on-billboard-top-country-albums-chart/|access-date=2021-02-28| website= [[KFDI]].com |publisher= Country 101.3 KFDI | language=en-US}}</ref> Wallen's second album, ''[[Dangerous: The Double Album]]'', was released in January 2021, and in February 2021 became the only country album in the 64-year history of the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] to spend its first seven weeks at No. 1.<ref>{{Cite magazine| last= Caulfield| first=Keith|date=February 28, 2021 |title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' Becomes Only Country Album to Spend First Seven Weeks at No. 1 on Billboard 200| url= https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/9532572/morgan-wallen-dangerous-tops-billboard-200-seven-weeks| access-date=2021-02-28|  magazine= Billboard|language=en}}</ref> It spent its first ten weeks at number one, the first album to do so since [[Whitney Houston]]'s ''[[Whitney (album)|Whitney]]'' in 1987.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Sisario|first=Ben|date=March 22, 2021|title=Morgan Wallen Tops Chart for a 10th Week| url= https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/22/arts/music/morgan-wallen-dangerous-billboard.html |archive-url= https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20211228/https://www.nytimes.com/2021/03/22/arts/music/morgan-wallen-dangerous-billboard.html |archive-date= 2021-12-28 |url-access= limited|access-date=2021-04-06| website=[[The New York Times]] |language=en}}{{cbignore}}</ref> The album included singles \"[[More Than My Hometown]]\", \"[[7 Summers]]\", and \"[[Wasted on You (Morgan Wallen song)|Wasted on You]]\".<ref name=\"Billboard-Feb 2021\">{{Cite magazine|title=Morgan Wallen on Country Digital Song Sales| url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/morgan-wallen/chart-history/cdt/| access-date=2021-02-28| magazine= Billboard}}</ref>\n\nHis third studio album, ''[[One Thing at a Time]]'' (2023), topped the ''Billboard'' 200 for 19 non-consecutive weeks, with all of its 36 tracks entering the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]]. This broke the record for most songs by an artist on the chart at one time.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Trust|first=Greg|date=March 13, 2023|title=Morgan Wallen Charts Single-Week Record 36 Songs on Hot 100 \u2013 Every Track From 'One Thing at a Time'|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/chart-beat/morgan-wallen-single-week-hot-100-record-36-songs-one-thing-at-a-time-1235285241/|magazine=Billboard|access-date=April 24, 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230313175534/https://www.billboard.com/music/chart-beat/morgan-wallen-single-week-hot-100-record-36-songs-one-thing-at-a-time-1235285241/|archive-date=March 13, 2023|url-status=live}}</ref> The single \"[[Last Night (Morgan Wallen song)|Last Night]]\" peaked atop the Hot 100 in 2023, becoming Wallen's first single to do so, and later set the record for the most weeks at number one for a non-collaboration song (sixteen weeks), as well as tying for the second most weeks of all time and topping the year-end chart. He has received several awards including an [[Academy of Country Music Awards|Academy of Country Music Award]] and fourteen [[Billboard Music Awards|''Billboard'' Music Awards]].<ref>{{Cite web |last=BBMAs |date=2023-11-13 |title=Country Music Superstar Morgan Wallen to Perform |url=https://www.billboardmusicawards.com/2023/11/country-music-superstar-morgan-wallen-to-perform/ |access-date=2024-02-14 |website=Billboard Music Awards |language=en}}</ref>\n{{toc limit|3}}\n\n==Early life and education==\nMorgan Cole Wallen was born on May 13, 1993, in [[Sneedville, Tennessee]], to Tommy and Lesli Wallen.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Randell|first=Louise|date=February 4, 2021|title=Everything we know about Morgan Wallen's parents| url= https://www.stylesrant.com/everything-we-know-about-morgan-wallen-parents/ |access-date=February 28, 2021| website=StylesRant.com |language= en-US}}</ref> Tommy served for a time as a local church pastor,<ref name=\"NY 2020\">{{cite magazine | last=Sanneh | first=Kelefa| authorlink=Kelefa Sanneh | title=How Morgan Wallen Became the Most Wanted Man in Country | magazine= [[The New Yorker]] | date=December 17, 2020 | url= https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2020/12/28/how-morgan-wallen-became-the-most-wanted-man-in-country | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref> while Lesli worked as a teacher. In his teens, the family moved south to [[Knox County, Tennessee|Knox County]], where he graduated from [[Gibbs High School (Corryton, Tennessee)|Gibbs High School]].<ref name=\"Deming\">{{cite web | last=Deming | first=Mark | title=Morgan Wallen Biography, Songs, & Albums | website=AllMusic| url= https://www.allmusic.com/artist/morgan-wallen-mn0003351348/biography | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref> He was a [[pitcher]] and [[shortstop]] for the school's [[baseball]] team, and hoped to continue in college, but tore his [[ulnar collateral ligament]] his senior year.<ref name=\"nash\">{{cite web|last=Casey|first=Jim|date=March 13, 2017|title=Who's New: Morgan Wallen|url=https://www.thecountrydaily.com/2017/03/13/whos-new-morgan-wallen-2/|access-date=February 28, 2021|work=The Country Daily}}</ref>\n\nAs a child, Wallen took piano and violin lessons. He was raised on a diverse musical playlist, with his father exposing him to [[classic rock]] mainstays. In his teens, he gravitated towards bands like [[Breaking Benjamin]] and [[Nickelback]], as well as rappers like [[Lil Wayne]].<ref name=\"bb20\"/>\n\nWallen has characterized his early adulthood as adrift; he worked in [[landscaping]] after high school and was disappointed by his inability to continue his baseball career.<ref name=\"NY 2020\"/> He re-approached his interest in music and began learning guitar.<ref name=\"bb20\"/> He had grown to love country music, especially artists like [[Keith Whitley]] and [[Eric Church]], and he modeled his sound after that lineage.<ref name=\"bb20\"/>\n\n==Career==\n\n===Early career and ''The Voice'' (2014\u20132017)===\nIn 2014, Wallen competed on [[The Voice (American TV series) season 6|season 6]] of the music competition program ''[[The Voice (American TV series)|The Voice]]''. He auditioned with the song \"[[Collide (Howie Day song)|Collide]]\" by [[Howie Day]]. Judges [[Shakira]] and [[Usher (musician)|Usher]] complimented his stylings, and Wallen joined Usher's team. He was later taken by [[Adam Levine]]'s team after his second round, and later eliminated during the playoffs.<ref name=\"nash\"/> Wallen was disappointed by the setback, but doubled down on his ambition: \"Some things in life are out of your control. Being the best you can be isn't. I didn't feel like I was the best I could have been. So I practiced harder\".<ref name=\"bb20\"/> Still, ''The Voice'' was instrumental in raising Wallen's profile, and he began to establish connections in the [[music industry]].<ref name=\"Deming\"/>\n\nWhile in California to appear on ''The Voice'', Wallen began working with Sergio Sanchez of [[Atom Smash]], a vocal coach on the program. Wallen relocated to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] to further his career, and he and Sanchez started a temporary band: Morgan Wallen & Them Shadows.<ref name=\"Deming\"/> Sanchez introduced Wallen to Bill Ray and [[Paul Trust]] of [[Panacea Records]].<ref name=\"carolina\">{{cite web|url=https://carolinacountrymusicfest.com/artist/morgan-wallen/ |title= Morgan Wallen Artist Bio| work= carolinacountrymusicfest.com | publisher= [[Carolina Country Music Fest]]|access-date=May 6, 2020}}</ref> In 2015, Wallen signed to [[Panacea Records]] where he was joined by Dominic Frost on guitar and released the [[Stand Alone (EP)|''Stand Alone'' (EP)]] on August 24, 2015. \"[[Spin You Around]]\" was Wallen's debut single under Panacea Records; it was later certified double platinum by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]] (RIAA) in 2021.<ref>{{Cite web| title= Gold & Platinum| url= https://www.riaa.com/gold-platinum/?tab_active=default-award&se=spin+you+around#search_section|access-date=2021-04-30| website= RIAA.com| publisher= Recording Industry Association of America|language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nIn 2015, Wallen's manager, Dirk Hemsath of Working Group Artist Management, sent a demo of Wallen to [[Big Loud|Big Loud Shirt]]'s Seth England, who had Wallen audition for his partners in [[Big Loud|Big Loud Records]]. They signed Wallen to the label and the publishing company,<ref name=\"carolina\"/> who began pairing his songs with other artists. That year, he released his debut single \"[[The Way I Talk]]\";<ref>{{Cite web| last= Pierce| first= Susan|date=November 20, 2018| title=With three hit singles, Morgan Wallen's music has been 'Up Down' and all over the charts| url= https://www.timesfreepress.com/news/chattanooganow/music/story/2018/nov/20/seeing-world-through-whiskey-glasses/483381/|access-date= February 28, 2021| website= timesfreepress.com}}</ref> his first [[music video]] for the song followed in 2017.<ref>{{cite web| url= http://www.soundslikenashville.com/news/morgan-wallen-celebrates-upbringing-video-way-talk/| title= Morgan Wallen Celebrates Upbringing in Video for 'The Way I Talk'|last=Brickey|first=Kelly|date=April 9, 2017|work=Sounds Like Nashville|access-date=April 23, 2017}}</ref> Wallen co-wrote the [[A Thousand Horses]]'s single \"Preachin' to the Choir\",<ref name=\"nash\"/> [[Dallas Smith]]'s \"The Fall\",<ref>{{Cite web|title=Dallas Smith - The Fall|url=https://newcountrysongs.com/dallas-smith/the-fall/|website=New Country Songs}}</ref> as well as [[Jason Aldean]]'s \"[[You Make It Easy]]\" with [[Florida Georgia Line]]'s [[Tyler Hubbard]], [[Brian Kelley]], and [[Jordan Schmidt]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/jason-aldean-you-make-it-easy-lyrics/|title=Lyrics uncovered: Jason Aldean, 'You Make It Easy'|work=Taste of Country|date=January 30, 2018 |access-date=February 14, 2018}}</ref> He joined Florida Georgia Line on their [[Dig Your Roots Tour]].<ref name=\"nash\"/> He collaborated with the group on the single \"[[Up Down (Morgan Wallen song)|Up Down]]\", his first song to reach the top five of ''Billboard''{{'}}s [[Hot Country Songs]] chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine|title=Morgan Wallen| url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/morgan-wallen/chart-history/lus/| access-date=February 28, 2021| magazine=Billboard}}</ref>\n\n===Mainstream success (2018\u2013present)===\n[[File:Morgan Wallen Concert November 13.jpg|thumb|Wallen performing in 2021]]\n\nAt the outset of his career, Wallen underwent a personal stylistic shift, adopting a distinctive [[Mullet (haircut)|mullet]] and a look that [[Kelefa Sanneh]], profiling Wallen's rise in a piece for ''[[The New Yorker]]'', described as \"[[Everyman]] rock star\" and \"not just a singer but a character\".<ref name=\"NY 2020\"/> Wallen had decided to adopt the retro hairdo after seeing a younger photo of his father with the cut.<ref name=\"bb20\"/> Wallen's debut studio album, ''[[If I Know Me (album)|If I Know Me]]'', was released on April 27, 2018,<ref>{{cite magazine | first= Jon | last= Freeman |date= June 19, 2018 | url= https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/how-up-down-singer-morgan-wallen-turned-his-accent-into-an-honest-country-voice-666096/ | magazine= Rolling Stone| title=How Up Down Singer Morgan Wallen Turned His Accent into an Honest Country Voice| accessdate=}}</ref> with its third single, \"[[Whiskey Glasses]]\", becoming his biggest success yet.<ref>{{Cite web| \nlast= SMF|date=2019-04-19| title= Morgan Wallen's \"Whiskey Glasses\" Lyrics Meaning| url= https://www.songmeaningsandfacts.com/morgan-wallens-whiskey-glasses-lyrics-meaning/|access-date=2021-02-28|website=Song Meanings and Facts|language=en-US}}</ref> The song reached the top spot on both the Hot Country Songs and [[Country Airplay]] charts; it also marked his top 40 appearance on the all-genre [[Billboard Hot 100|Hot 100]] ranking, where it placed at number 17. It was ''Billboard''{{'}}s 2019 top Hot Country song and Top Country Airplay song.<ref>{{Cite web |last= Dukes|first=Billy|date=June 4, 2019| title=Morgan Wallen's 'Whiskey Glasses' Hits No. 1 on Airplay Charts| url=https://tasteofcountry.com/morgan-wallen-whiskey-glasses-no-1-radio-airplay/|access-date=February 28, 2021|website=Taste of Country| language=en}}</ref> Sanneh characterized \"Whiskey Glasses\" as his [[signature song]] and a \"perfectly constructed ode to a woman and a drink, lost and found, respectively\".<ref name=\"NY 2020\"/> In 2019, Wallen joined Florida Georgia Line on their [[Can't Say I Ain't Country Tour]].<ref>{{cite web| url= https://www.onecountry.com/country-artists/florida-georgia-line-announce-tour-dates/| title= Florida Georgia Line Announce Can't Say I Ain't Country Tour with Dan + Shay| last= Konicki| first= Lisa| date= January 9, 2019| website= Onecountry.com| access-date= February 2, 2019| archive-date= November 27, 2020| archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20201127151634/https://www.onecountry.com/country-artists/florida-georgia-line-announce-tour-dates/| url-status= dead}}</ref> His next single, \"[[Chasin' You]]\", was serviced to radio in July 2019 and peaked at number two on the Hot Country Songs chart;<ref>{{cite web| url=http://www.nashcountrydaily.com/2019/07/09/morgan-wallen-to-release-smoldering-new-single-chasin-you-listen/|title=Morgan Wallen to Release Smoldering New Single, \"Chasin' You\" [Listen]| last=Casey |first= Jim|website=Nash Country Daily| publisher=Cumulus Media| date=July 9, 2019}}</ref><ref name=\"Billboard-Feb 2021\" /> like its predecessor, it captured the top spot on the overall year-end tally for 2020.<ref name=\"bb20\"/> In August 2020, ''If I Know Me'' reached No. 1 on the Top Country Albums chart after a record-breaking 114 weeks.\n\nWallen's profile continued to rise, with a growing following on platforms like [[TikTok]], and he developed into an unwitting [[sex symbol]].<ref name=\"NY 2020\"/> Wallen appeared on the cover of ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'', whose headline read: \"Is Morgan Wallen Country's Next Global Star?\"<ref name=\"bb20\">{{Cite magazine| date=2021-01-14|title=Is Morgan Wallen Country's Next Global Star?|url= https://www.billboard.com/music/country/morgan-wallen-dangerous-billboard-cover-story-interview-2021-9510855/|access-date=2021-02-15|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> At the start of the [[COVID-19 pandemic]], Wallen found himself with more time to write and record material, which developed into his sophomore album, the double-disc ''[[Dangerous: The Double Album]]'' (2021),<ref name=\"Dangerous\">{{cite web| last= Dukes|first=Billy|date=November 11, 2020|title=Morgan Wallen Announces New 'Dangerous' Double Album, Featuring Chris Stapleton| url= https://tasteofcountry.com/morgan-wallen-dangerous-album/|access-date=November 12, 2020|work=Taste of Country}}</ref> which showcases a mix of country and [[Contemporary R&B|R&B]]/pop [[ballad]]ry.<ref name= \"Deming\"/> ''Dangerous'' was an immediate blockbuster: it debuted atop the US [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] and the [[Canadian Albums Chart]];<ref name=\"BB200\">{{cite magazine |url= https://www.billboard.com/artist/morgan-wallen/chart-history/tlp/ |title=Morgan Wallen Chart History: Billboard 200 |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=February 4, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine| url= https://www.billboard.com/artist/morgan-wallen/chart-history/cna/ |title= Morgan Wallen Chart History: Canadian Albums |magazine= Billboard |access-date=August 25, 2020}}</ref> it would remain atop the Canadian chart for four consecutive weeks, and the US chart for six consecutive weeks, marking the first new album from a country artist to do that since [[Garth Brooks]]' ''[[The Chase (Garth Brooks album)|The Chase]]'' in 1992.<ref name=\"Six\" /><ref>{{cite magazine| title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' No. 1 for Fifth Week on Billboard 200 While 'If I Know Me' Hits Top 10 for First Time| url= https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9526109/morgan-wallen-dangerous-tops-billboard-200-for-fifth-week/ |first=Keith| last= Caulfield| magazine= Billboard |date= February 14, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' Makes It Three Weeks at No. 1 on Billboard 200 Chart| url= https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9519004/morgan-wallen-dangerous-tops-billboard-200-three-weeks-straight/#:~:text=Morgan%20Wallen%27s%20Dangerous%3A%20The,the%20list%20in%20eight%20years.|first=Keith|last=Caulfield|magazine= Billboard |date=January 31, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine| title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' Spends Fourth Week at No. 1 on Billboard 200 Albums Chart| url= https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9522648/morgan-wallen-dangerous-tops-billboard-200-fourth-week|first=Keith|last=Caulfield|magazine= Billboard| date=February 7, 2021}}</ref> Its singles\u2014\"[[More Than My Hometown]]\", \"[[7 Summers]]\", \"[[Sand in My Boots]]\" and \"[[Wasted on You (Morgan Wallen song)|Wasted on You]]\"\u2014were record-breaking [[hit single|hit song]]s that pushed Wallen farther into the national conversation. \"7 Summers\" earned him his first top 10 on the Hot 100, debuting and peaking at number six,<ref>{{cite web| url= https://www.countrynow.com/morgan-wallen-shatters-records-with-7-summers/amp/| title= Morgan Wallen Shatters Records With '7 Summers'| work= Country Now| last= Black| first= Lauren Jo| date= August 19, 2020| access-date= August 19, 2020| archive-date= November 30, 2020| archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20201130204256/https://www.countrynow.com/morgan-wallen-shatters-records-with-7-summers/amp/| url-status= dead}}</ref> and was also chosen by ''[[Time (magazine)|Time]]'' as one of the best songs of the year.<ref>{{Cite magazine|title=The 10 Best Songs of 2020|url=https://time.com/5914984/best-songs-2020/|access-date= December 10, 2020|magazine=Time}}</ref> Wallen soon became the first artist to ever chart six songs within the top 10 of Hot Country Songs chart at the same time in the week after his album's release;<ref>{{cite magazine | url= https://bulletins.billboard.com/country/country_update_2021_0119.pdf | title= Billboard Country Update: On the Charts | publisher=  | magazine= Billboard | date= January 19, 2021 | access-date= January 20, 2021 | author= Jim Asker | pages= 4 | archive-date= January 28, 2021 | archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20210128005040/https://bulletins.billboard.com/country/country_update_2021_0119.pdf | url-status= dead }}</ref> likewise, the album charted 23 tracks on the [[Canadian Hot 100]],<ref name= \"Canada Hot 100\">{{cite magazine| title=Morgan Wallen Chart History (Canadian Hot 100) |url= https://www.billboard.com/artist/morgan-wallen/chart-history/can/ |magazine= Billboard |access-date=February 4, 2021}}</ref> and 19 tracks on the Hot 100 in the US.<ref name=\"Billboard Hot 100\">{{cite magazine|title=Morgan Wallen Chart History (Hot 100) |url= https://www.billboard.com/artist/morgan-wallen/chart-history/hsi/ |magazine= Billboard |access-date=February 4, 2021}}</ref>\n\n====Use of racial slur====\n\nOn February 2, 2021, [[TMZ]] released a video recorded on January 31 showing Wallen using the racial slur \"[[nigger]]\" to one of his friends after a night out.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Williams |first1=Andrea |title=Morgan Wallen Is Exactly What Country Music Wanted \u2026 Now What? |url=https://www.vulture.com/2021/02/essay-morgan-wallen-racism-controversy.html |website=Vulture |access-date=23 February 2021 |date=4 February 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.gq.com/story/suspending-morgan-wallen-was-a-start-now-comes-the-hard-part | title=Suspending Morgan Wallen Was a Start. Now Comes the Hard Part | date=February 5, 2021 }}</ref> He issued a statement shortly after and apologized.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Calvario|first=Liz|date=February 2, 2021|title=Morgan Wallen Apologizes for Using the N-Word After Rowdy Night Out|url=https://www.etonline.com/morgan-wallen-apologizes-for-using-the-n-word-after-night-out-with-pals-159986|access-date=February 3, 2021|website=[[Entertainment Tonight]]|language=en-US}}</ref> Several radio stations temporarily removed Wallen's music from airplay on their stations, and his songs were removed from [[Apple Music]], [[Pandora (streaming service)|Pandora]] and [[Spotify]] featured playlists.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Morgan Wallen's Music Removed From iHeart's Radio Stations and Others Following Racial Slur|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/9520243/morgan-wallen-removed-iheartradio-cumulus-racial-slur-fallout/|access-date=February 3, 2021|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Willman|first1=Chris|date=February 3, 2021|title=Country Radio Quickly Removing Morgan Wallen From Playlists After Racial Slur|url=https://variety.com/2021/music/news/morgan-wallen-country-radio-removed-racial-slur-1234899010/|access-date=February 3, 2021|magazine=[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]|language=en-US}}</ref> [[CMT (American TV channel)|CMT]] and the [[Country Music Association]] removed Wallen's appearances from their platforms, and his record label [[Big Loud]] (and partner [[Republic Records]]) suspended its recording contract with him indefinitely.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Millman|first1=Ethan|date=February 3, 2021|title=Morgan Wallen's Record Deal 'Suspended Indefinitely' Following Racial Slur Video|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/morgan-wallen-record-label-suspended-1123242/|access-date=February 3, 2021|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Limbong|first=Andrew|date=February 3, 2021|title=Country Star Morgan Wallen Suspended By Label, Dropped By Radio, CMT After Using Slur|work=NPR|url=https://www.npr.org/2021/02/03/963664999/country-star-morgan-wallen-suspended-by-label-dropped-by-radio-cmt-after-using-s|access-date=}}</ref> The [[Academy of Country Music]] announced that Wallen and the album ''[[Dangerous: The Double Album]]'' would be ineligible for the [[56th Academy of Country Music Awards|56th Annual]] [[Academy of Country Music Awards]].<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Grein |first1=Paul |title=Morgan Wallen Won't Be Eligible for 2021 ACM Awards After Racial Slur |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/awards/9520781/morgan-wallen-acm-awards-ineligible-racial-slur/ |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |date=February 3, 2021|access-date=February 4, 2021 |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Morgan Wallen Disqualified by Academy of Country Music for Upcoming Awards; One-Day Airplay Down 80%|url=https://variety.com/2021/music/news/morgan-wallen-disqualified-acm-awards-cma-radio-play-drops-1234899952/|author=Chris Willman|website=Variety|date=February 3, 2021|access-date=February 4, 2021}}</ref> On February 10, Wallen shot an apology video in which he asked his fans not to defend him.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Hudak|first=Joseph|date=2021-02-11|title=Morgan Wallen to Fans: Don't Defend Me|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/morgan-wallen-apology-video-1126831/|access-date=2021-02-15|magazine=Rolling Stone}}</ref>\n\nIn April 2021, Wallen donated $300,000 to the [[Black Music Action Coalition]] in the names of 20 people who had counseled him following the incident. Those individuals were given the option to funnel their respective $15,000 donations to a charity of their choice, or keep the money within the BMAC.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Ruggieri|first=Melissa|title=The real story of Morgan Wallen's $500K pledge to Black groups, and how the money got distributed|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/entertainment/music/2021/09/22/morgan-wallen-kept-his-pledge-donate-money-black-serving-groups/5788855001/|access-date=2021-11-23|website=USA Today|language=en-US}}</ref> Wallen publicly spoke of his comments on ''[[Good Morning America]]'' on July 23, where he said that \"he was around some of his friends, and they say dumb stuff together\" and said that \"he was wrong\" to express those words.<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Kaufman |first1=Gil |title=Morgan Wallen Thought His Use of Racial Slur Was 'Playful,' Admits It Was 'Ignorant' & 'Wrong' |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/9605488/morgan-wallen-talks-racial-slur-gma-video/ |access-date=24 July 2021 |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |date=24 July 2021}}</ref> Wallen's songs returned to country radio in August when his single \"[[Sand in My Boots]]\" was released.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicmayhemmagazine.com/morgan-wallen-officially-returning-to-country-radio-with-new-single-sand-in-my-boots/|title=Morgan Wallen Officially Returning To Country Radio With New Single \"Sand In My Boots\"|access-date=September 22, 2021|website=Music Mayhem Magazine|date=August 20, 2021 |language=en-US}}</ref> He was nominated for Favorite Male Country Artist and Favorite Country Album for the 2021 [[American Music Awards]], but was not invited to attend the ceremony, and was consequently unable to accept any awards if he won, which he did not.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.foxnews.com/entertainment/morgan-wallen-banned-american-music-award-country-nominations|title=Morgan Wallen banned from American Music Awards, still nominated for country music categories|access-date=October 29, 2021|website=FoxNews.com|date=October 29, 2021 |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n====Continued success====\n[[File:Morgan_Wallen_performing_in_Salt_Lake_City.png|thumb|Wallen performing in 2022]]\n\nThough his public image took a hit, Wallen\u2019s popularity increased.<ref name= \"USA\">{{Cite web|last= Oliver |first= David|title=Morgan Wallen used a racist slur but his popularity is skyrocketing. How did we get here? |url= https://www.usatoday.com/story/entertainment/music/2021/02/10/morgan-wallen-country-music-popular-after-racist-slur-what-it-means/4441395001/ |access-date= 2021-02-18|website=USA Today}}</ref> In the week following the controversy, album sales of ''Dangerous'' surged. In some cases, the physical as well as digital album sales went up over 100% in the week following the controversy.<ref name= \"KSAT&quot;&quot;\">{{Cite web |last= Hall |first=Kristin M. | agency= Associated Press|date=2021-02-08| title= Album sales surge for Morgan Wallen after racist comment| url= https://www.ksat.com/entertainment/2021/02/08/album-sales-surge-for-morgan-wallen-after-racist-comment/ |website=KSAT.com | publisher= |access-date=2021-02-15}}</ref> He remained atop the ''Billboard'' charts for seven more weeks; ''If I Know Me'' even entered the top 10 for the first time.<ref>{{Cite magazine|title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' No. 1 for Fifth Week on Billboard 200 While 'If I Know Me' Hits Top 10 for First Time| url= https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9526109/morgan-wallen-dangerous-tops-billboard-200-for-fifth-week|access-date=2021-02-15| magazine=Billboard}}</ref> Over the ensuing years, ''Dangerous'' remained a juggernaut; Ben Sisario, writing in ''[[The New York Times]]'', dubbed it \"an unusually enduring hit\".<ref name=\"The New York Times 2022\">{{cite web | title=Morgan Wallen's Career Seemed Over. Now He's Broken a Billboard Record. | website=The New York Times | date=September 12, 2022 | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2022/09/12/arts/music/morgan-wallen-dangerous-billboard-chart-record.html | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref> It has continued to break chart records:<ref name=\"Six\">{{Cite magazine| title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' Hits Sixth Week at No. 1 on Billboard 200, Most for a Male Artist Since Drake's 'Views'| url= https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9529137/morgan-wallen-dangerous-tops-billboard-200-sixth-week| access-date=2021-02-21| magazine= Billboard}}</ref> it was the best-performing album of 2021,<ref name=\"Vitagliano 2021\"/> and in 2022, the album broke the record for the most weeks in the top 10 on the ''Billboard 200'' chart among albums by a singular artist, surpassing a goal set a half-century before.<ref name=\"Caulfield 2022\">{{cite web | last=Caulfield | first=Keith | title=Morgan Wallen's 'Dangerous' Breaks Top 10 Longevity Record on Billboard 200 Chart | website=Billboard.com | date= September 11, 2022 | url= https://www.billboard.com/music/chart-beat/morgan-wallen-dangerous-double-album-billboard-200-chart-longevity-record-1235137231/ | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref> ''Dangerous'' was awarded Album of the Year at the Academy of Country Music;<ref>{{cite web |url= https://www.acmcountry.com/noms |title=Winners| website= acmcountry.com |publisher=Academy of Country Music |access-date=1 June 2022}}</ref> Wallen also won Favorite Male Artist and Favorite Album at the inaugural Country Now Awards.<ref name=\"Country Now-2021\" />\n\nWallen has continued to release new music, and has remained a popular draw on the road. ''The Dangerous Tour'' of arenas and amphitheaters was completely sold-out.<ref name=\"Vitagliano 2021\">{{cite web | last=Vitagliano | first=Joe | title=Morgan Wallen Tour is Nearly Sold Out\u2013Over 705k Tickets Sold So Far | website=American Songwriter | date=December 7, 2021 | url=https://americansongwriter.com/morgan-wallen-tour-is-nearly-sold-out-over-705k-tickets-sold-so-far/ | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref><ref name=\"Nicholson 2022\">{{cite magazine | last=Nicholson | first=Jessica | title=Morgan Wallen Brings Hits, Jason Aldean & More to Round Out Trio of Nashville Shows | magazine=Billboard | date=March 19, 2022 | url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/morgan-wallen-nashville-concerts-recap-1235046165/ | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref> His single \"[[You Proof]]\" became his second Hot 100 hit and first to reach the top five; both \"You Proof\" and \"[[Thought You Should Know (Morgan Wallen song)|Thought You Should Know]]\" topped the country charts. Wallen also collaborated with rapper [[Lil Durk]] on the song \"[[Broadway Girls]]\", a top-15 hit on the Hot 100; he also performed the song live with Durk at MLK Freedom Fest in Nashville.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Hudak|first=Joseph|title=Morgan Wallen Joins Lil Durk Onstage at MLK Freedom Fest in Nashville|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/morgan-wallen-lil-durk-nashville-broadway-girls-1286003/|date=January 15, 2022|access-date=January 16, 2022|magazine=Rolling Stone}}</ref> Wallen was a co-writer on the [[Tyler Joe Miller]] single \"[[Wild as Her]]\", released in February 2022, and the [[Keith Urban]] single \"[[Brown Eyes Baby]], released in July 2022.<ref name =\"AllMusicb\">{{cite web|title=\"Wild as Her\" \u2013 Tyler Joe Miller|url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/wild-as-her-mw0003678677|work=[[AllMusic]]|accessdate=April 3, 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicmayhemmagazine.com/listen-keith-urban-releases-new-single-brown-eyes-baby-co-penned-by-morgan-wallen/|title=Keith Urban Releases New Single \"Brown Eyes Baby,\" Co-Penned By Morgan Wallen [Listen]|date=July 8, 2022}}</ref> In December 2022, Wallen released a sampler EP titled ''One Thing at a Time'', featuring three songs he had been working on up until this point, titled \"One Thing at a Time\", \"Tennessee Fan\" and \"Days That End in Why\".<ref>{{cite magazine |url= https://www.billboard.com/music/country/morgan-wallen-stream-it-now-1235179772/| title=Morgan Wallen's 'One Thing at a Time' Sampler: Stream It Now| last=Nicholson| first= Jessica| magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |date=December 2, 2022|access-date=December 3, 2022}}</ref> In 2023, Wallen expanded to stadiums with his One Night at a Time World Tour.<ref name=\"Mier 2022\">{{cite magazine | last=Mier | first= Tom\u00e1s| title=Morgan Wallen Will Take 2023 'One Night at a Time' on a Massive World Tour | magazine=Rolling Stone | date=December 6, 2022 | url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/morgan-wallen-2023-tour-dates-1234639735/ | access-date=December 7, 2022}}</ref> Wallen released his third studio album ''[[One Thing at a Time]]'' on March 3, 2023.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicmayhemmagazine.com/morgan-wallen-announces-36-track-album-one-thing-at-a-time-featuring-duets-with-eric-church-hardy-ernest/|title=Morgan Wallen Announces 36-Track Album 'One Thing At A Time' Featuring Duets With Eric Church, Hardy & Ernest|website=Music Mayhem Magazine|last=Wendowski|first=Andrew|date=January 30, 2023|access-date=January 31, 2023}}</ref>\n\nOn April 23, 2023, at [[Vaught\u2013Hemingway Stadium]] in [[Oxford, Mississippi]], just minutes before he was set to perform, Wallen announced that he could not perform due to losing his voice. Fans were directed to receive refunds at their points of purchase.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/news/2023/04/25/morgan-wallen-mississippi-concert-canceled-lawsuit-refunds-more/70150025007/#|title=Morgan Wallen cancels concert in Oxford|access-date=April 25, 2023|website=[[The Tennessean]]|date=April 25, 2023 |language=en-US}}</ref> In May 2023, Wallen was featured on the song \"[[Stand by Me (Lil Durk song)|Stand by Me]]\" from [[Lil Durk]]'s eighth studio album, ''[[Almost Healed]]''. Wallen was a co-writer on the 2023 single \"[[Fixer Upper (Dallas Smith song)|Fixer Upper]]\" by [[Dallas Smith]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://frontporchmusic.ca/dallas-smiths-new-single-fixer-upper/|title=Dallas Smith's New Single \"Fixer Upper\": A Heartfelt Journey of Self-Work in Relationships|date=September 29, 2023|website=Front Porch Music|access-date=October 4, 2023}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://americansongwriter.com/dallas-smith-drops-fixer-upper-and-crzy-ahead-of-album-release/|title=Dallas Smith Drops \"Fixer Upper\" and \"CRZY\" Ahead of Album Release|first=Danielle|last=Taylor|magazine=[[American Songwriter]]|access-date=November 6, 2023}}</ref>\n\nOn January 26, 2024, [[Panacea Records]] released a deluxe 10th anniversary edition of Morgan Wallen's 2015 EP ''Stand Alone'' that included eight previously unreleased songs. These songs were recorded in the same sessions as the original ''Stand Alone'' songs. Before the release of the 10th anniversary album, Wallen released a statement on his Instagram page saying that the release of this album was happening \"against his wishes\".<ref>{{Cite web |date=2024-01-26 |title=Morgan Wallen Slams 'Greedy' Ex-Partners Issuing 'Terrible' Decade-Old Tracks; Indie Label Says 'We Believe Some of His Fans Will Love It' |url=https://www.yahoo.com/entertainment/morgan-wallen-slams-greedy-ex-041854886.html |access-date=2024-05-14 |website=Yahoo Entertainment |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nOn March 3, 2024, he shared performances as part of his Abbey Road Sessions and performed a new song titled \"[[Lies Lies Lies]]\".<ref>{{cite tweet|user=MorganWallen|number=1764399811757768839|title= Recorded a new song, some favorites, and a cover with my band in London at Abbey Road Studios - you can find them on my YouTube now!|access-date=March 4, 2024}}</ref> On May 2, 2024, Wallen announced his next single entitled \"[[I Had Some Help]]\" with [[Post Malone]], which was released on May 10.<ref>{{cite tweet|user=postmalone|number=1786149057842344340|title=I Had Some Help. May 10th @MorganWallen|date=May 2, 2024|access-date=May 3, 2024}}</ref>\n\n==Legal and public health issues==\nIn May 2020, Wallen was arrested and charged with public intoxication and disorderly conduct after leaving [[Kid Rock]]'s bar in [[Nashville]], Tennessee, and he confessed via [[Twitter]] that he and a few friends were \"horse-playing with each other\" after a couple of bar stops, saying \"We didn't mean any harm, and we want to say sorry to any bar staff or anyone that was affected.\"<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.tennessean.com/story/news/local/2020/05/24/morgan-wallen-arrested-nashville-bar/5253959002/ |title=Country artist Morgan Wallen arrested after being kicked out of Kid Rock's bar, police say |work=The Tennessean |last=Tamburin |first=Adam |date=May 24, 2020 |access-date=August 13, 2024}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wkrn.com/news/crime-tracker/country-artist-morgan-wallen-arrested-after-incident-at-kid-rocks-honky-tonk/ |title=Country artist Morgan Wallen arrested after incident at Kid Rock\u2019s Honky Tonk |work=[[WKRN]].com |date=May 24, 2020 |access-date=August 13, 2024}}</ref>\n\nIn October 2020, during the [[COVID-19 pandemic in the United States|COVID-19 pandemic]], multiple videos were posted on TikTok showing Wallen ignoring [[Centers for Disease Control and Prevention|CDC]] guidelines (to lower the risk of catching and/or spreading COVID-19) in bars and other locations in the Tuscaloosa, Alabama area after attending a [[University of Alabama]] football game.  Wallen was shown partying maskless, not following social distancing guidelines, and kissing several women in these videos.  Wallen was criticized for his conduct, partly as his ex-girlfriend had recently given birth.  As a result of his actions, Wallen was cancelled as the musical guest on that week's episode of ''[[Saturday Night Live]]''; he ultimately performed in an episode two months later hosted by actor [[Jason Bateman]], in which Bateman, Wallen, and several cast members parody the incident and resulting fallout.<ref name=\"maskless partying 1\">{{cite web |last1=Aderoju |first1=Darlene |title=Morgan Wallen Faces Criticism After Partying amid Coronavirus Ahead of 'SNL' Appearance |url=https://people.com/country/morgan-wallen-snl-criticism-after-partying/ |website=People.com |publisher=People Magazine |access-date=March 15, 2024 |date=October 7, 2020}}</ref><ref name=\"maskless partying 2\">{{cite web |last1=Moniuszko |first1=Sara M. |title='SNL': Morgan Wallen stars in maskless partying skit months after his own COVID-19 scandal |url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/entertainment/tv/2020/12/06/snl-morgan-wallen-maskless-partying-skit-coronavirus-scandal/3847347001/ |website=USAToday.com |publisher=USA Today |access-date=March 15, 2024 |date=December 6, 2020}}</ref><ref name=\"maskless partying 3\">{{cite web |last1=Low |first1=Elaine |title=Morgan Wallen Under Scrutiny for Maskless Partying Ahead of 'SNL' Appearance |url=https://variety.com/2020/tv/news/morgan-wallen-saturday-night-live-covid-partying-1234795121/ |website=Variety.com |publisher=Variety |access-date=March 15, 2024 |date=October 6, 2020}}</ref><ref name=\"maskless partying 4\">{{cite web |last1=Levenson |first1=Eric |title='SNL' and Morgan Wallen joke about the show disinviting him for breaking Covid-19 protocols |url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/12/06/us/snl-morgan-wallen/index.html |website=CNN.com |publisher=CNN (Cable News Network) |access-date=March 15, 2024 |date=December 6, 2020}}</ref>\n\nOn April 7, 2024, Wallen was arrested after allegedly throwing a chair off the roof of [[Eric Church]]'s newly-opened bar on [[Broadway (Nashville, Tennessee)|Broadway]] in Nashville. He was charged with three counts of [[felony]] reckless endangerment and one count of [[misdemeanor]] disorderly conduct after the projectile landed near two police officers on the ground.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Fieldstadt |first1=Elisha |last2=Lenthang |first2=Marlene |title=Morgan Wallen arrested after throwing chair from rooftop of Nashville bar, police say |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/morgan-wallen-arrested-throwing-chair-rooftop-nashville-bar-police-say-rcna146810 |website=NBC News |access-date=April 8, 2024 |date=April 8, 2024}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nIn 2016, Wallen began a relationship with influencer KT Smith, and the couple got engaged several months later.<ref>{{Cite web |last=Santaflorentina |first=Hayley |date=2024-04-10 |title=Morgan Wallen's ex KT Smith speaks out amid reports her elopement was behind bar incident |url=https://www.nbcdfw.com/entertainment/entertainment-news/morgan-wallens-ex-kt-smith-speaks-out-amid-reports-her-elopement-was-behind-bar-incident/3510598/ |access-date=2024-09-25 |website=NBC 5 Dallas-Fort Worth |language=en-US}}</ref><ref name=\":0\">{{Cite web |last=Aizin |first=Rebecca |date=April 10, 2024 |title=Who Is Morgan Wallen's Ex-Girlfriend? All About KT Smith |url=https://people.com/who-is-kt-smith-morgan-wallen-ex-girlfriend-8628504 |access-date=2024-09-25 |website=[[Peoplemag|People]] |language=en}}</ref> In 2019, they separated, allegedly due to Wallen's infidelity, and welcomed a son, Indigo (b. 2020), together several months after their breakup.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://people.com/parents/morgan-wallen-celebrates-son-indigo-1st-birthday-with-ex-kt-smith/ | title=Morgan Wallen Celebrates Son Indigo Wilder's 1st Birthday with Ex KT Smith After Controversy | publisher=[[People (magazine)|People]] | date=July 12, 2021 | accessdate=July 19, 2022}}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://people.com/who-is-kt-smith-morgan-wallen-ex-girlfriend-8628504 | title=Who is Morgan Wallen's Ex-Girlfriend? All About KT Smith }}</ref><ref name=\":0\" /> Smith is now married to another man.<ref name=\":0\" /> Wallen has also been romantically linked with influencer [[Paige Lorenze]],<ref>{{cite web | url=https://925xtu.com/2022/10/03/morgan-wallens-famous-ex-girlfriend/ | title=Morgan Wallen's Famous Ex-Girlfriend Reveals the Interesting Reason They Broke up | date=October 3, 2022 }}</ref> and fellow country singer [[Megan Moroney]], who allegedly wrote her breakout song \"[[Tennessee Orange]]\" about him.<ref>{{cite magazine | url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/megan-moroney-addresses-morgan-wallen-romance-rumors-1235744155/ | title=Megan Moroney Finally Addresses Morgan Wallen Romance Rumors: 'We Were Not Just Friends' | magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] }}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.usmagazine.com/celebrity-news/news/singer-megan-moroney-finally-addresses-morgan-wallen-dating-rumors/ | title=Singer Megan Moroney Finally Addresses Morgan Wallen Dating Rumors }}</ref><ref>{{cite web | url=https://people.com/megan-moroney-breaks-silence-on-morgan-wallen-romance-8686842 | title=Megan Moroney Breaks Silence on Morgan Wallen Romance, Says They Were Never 'Exclusively Dating' }}</ref>\n\nOn June 1, 2024, Wallen opened Morgan Wallen's This Bar & Tennessee Kitchen, a six-story bar, restaurant and music venue, in downtown Nashville.<ref>{{cite magazine | url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/morgan-wallen-nashville-bar-opening-june-1-1235698251/ | title=Morgan Wallen's Nashville Bar Opening June 1 | magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] }}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|Morgan Wallen discography}}\n*''[[If I Know Me (album)|If I Know Me]]'' Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Charly_McClain","to":"Charly McClain"}],"pages":{"1690039":{"pageid":1690039,"ns":0,"title":"Charly McClain","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Charly McClain\n| image           = File:Charly McClain (2).JPG\n| caption         = Charly McClain performing at the [[Martin County Fair]] in [[Stuart, Florida]], March 9, 1989\n(Photo courtesy of Jeff Moore.)\n| birth_name      = Charlotte Denise McClain\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1956|3|26}}\n| birth_place     = [[Memphis, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| genre           = [[Country pop]]\n| occupation      = Singer\n| instrument      = Vocals\n| years_active    = 1976\u20131991\n| label           = {{hlist|[[Epic Records]]|[[Mercury Records]]}}\n| spouse = {{marriage|[[Wayne Massey]]|1984}}\n}}\n\n'''Charlotte Denise''' \"'''Charly'''\" '''McClain''' (born March 26, 1956)<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\">{{cite book|title=[[Encyclopedia of Popular Music|The Guinness Who's Who of Country Music]]|editor=[[Colin Larkin (writer)|Colin Larkin]]|publisher=[[Guinness Publishing]]|date=1993|edition=First|isbn=0-85112-726-6|page=248}}</ref> is an American [[country music]] singer, best known for a string of hits during the 1980s. McClain's biggest hits include \"[[Who's Cheatin' Who]]\", \"[[Sleepin' with the Radio On]]\", and \"[[Radio Heart (Charly McClain song)|Radio Heart]]\".\n\n==Early life==\nMcClain was born in [[Memphis, Tennessee]], United States,<ref name=\"AMG\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/charly-mcclain-mn0000772541/biography|title=Charly McClain &#124; Biography & History|website=[[AllMusic]]|access-date=8 August 2021}}</ref> to Virginia (n\u00e9e Wiggins; 1934\u20132009) and Niles McClain. The nickname \"Charly\" would come from the neighborhood friends that she played with as a child.<ref name=\"AMG\"/> McClain used it when she began her career playing hotel [[lobby (room)|lounges]].<ref name=\"AMG\"/> Her first experience recording was when father Niles had [[tuberculosis]] when she was eight.<ref name=\"AMG\"/> As she was under age to comply with [[hospital]] visiting policy, she had to communicate with him through a [[tape recorder]].<ref name=\"AMG\"/> That inspired her interest in recording.<ref name=\"AMG\"/> She began her musical career at age 12 performing with her brother Mike and their band, Charlotte & the Volunteers. The band  performed together for the next six years.\n\nHer first TV appearance was on the local [[WBBJ-TV|WBBJ]] morning show in [[Jackson, Tennessee]]. By the age of 17, she was a regular on the club circuit, and appeared at the [[Memphis, Tennessee|Memphis]] show ''Mid-South Jamboree'' from 1973\u20131975.\n\n==Recording career==\n{{BLP sources section|date=November 2022}}\n\n===Steady rise===\nAt the age of 20, McClain signed her first recording contract with [[Epic Records]] in 1976. McClain's distinct vocal sound provided an edge in recognizability\u2014as did her attractive appearance.<ref name=\"AMG\"/> McClain debuted in late 1976 with her first [[Promotional recording|single]], \"Lay Down,\" which peaked at No. 67 on the [[Hot Country Songs|Billboard Country Chart]]. McClain's initial singles in 1976 and 1977, from her debut [[album]] ''Here's Charly McClain,'' failed to appear highly on the country chart. McClain's second album, ''Let Me Be Your Baby,'' was released in 1978. She hit country's Top Ten for the first time in 1978 with \"[[That's What You Do to Me]],\" <ref name=\"AMG\"/> followed by two other Top 25 hits, \"Let Me Be Your Baby,\" and \"Take Me Back.\"\n\nIn 1979 McClain released ''Alone Too Long'', which included the Top-20 hits \"When A Love Ain't Right\" and \"You're a Part of Me\". The ''Women Get Lonely'' album followed in 1980, featuring the Top 10 hit \"[[Men (Charly McClain song)|Men]]\",<ref name=\"AMG\"/> which peaked at No. 7 in 1980, and the Top-20 duet with [[Johnny Rodriguez]], \"I Hate the Way I Love It.\" However, breakthrough success still eluded McClain.\n\n===Achieving success===\nMcClain hit No. 1 on the country chart in 1981 with \"[[Who's Cheatin' Who]]\".<ref name=AOL>{{Cite web |url=http://music.aol.com/artist/charly-mcclain/biography/1001431 |title=Charly McClain biography at AOL.com |access-date=2008-03-30 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100413194048/http://music.aol.com/artist/charly-mcclain/biography/1001431 |archive-date=2010-04-13 |url-status=dead }}</ref> In 1981, McClain scored three Top-10 hits off her ''Surround Me with Love'' album: the [[Surround Me with Love|title track]], \"[[Sleepin' with the Radio On]]\", and \"[[The Very Best Is You]]\".<ref name=\"AMG\"/> McClain's albums were beginning to become more successful as well. Her ''Who's Cheatin' Who'' album peaked at No. 28 on the ''Top Country Albums'' chart, and her 1981 album, ''Surround Me With Love'' went to number 9.\n\nIn 1983, McClain hit No. 1 again with her [[Mickey Gilley]] duet \"[[Paradise Tonight]].\"<ref name=\"AMG\"/><ref name=AOL/> McClain's and Gilley's duet partnership became so successful, they released a duet album the following year titled ''It Takes Believers.'' The record contained the Top-5 hit, \"[[Candy Man (Roy Orbison song)|Candy Man]]\" (No. 5 on the Billboard Country Chart), and the top 20 hit, \"The Right Stuff\".\n\nMcClain also acted; she appeared as a guest star on such shows as ''[[Hart to Hart]]''<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> (in 1981 episode titled \"Rhinestone Harts\") and ''[[CHiPs]]'' (in 1983 episode \"Country Action\"). McClain's lonely life on the road was also chronicled in a 1981 [[HBO]] special titled ''So You Want to Be a Star.''\n\nAfter having a series of hit singles in 1984, McClain released another best-selling album, ''Radio Heart'' in 1985. The album's [[Radio Heart (Charly McClain song)|title track]] became a No. 1 Country hit in 1985; McClain's last No. 1 to date. The album also spawned two other Top-10 hits that year. McClain married former soap star [[Wayne Massey]] in 1984, and their duet \"[[With Just One Look in Your Eyes]]\" reached number five.<ref name=AOL/> The third single off the album was also a duet with Massey. It was titled \"[[You Are My Music, You Are My Song]]\". The ''Radio Heart'' album peaked at No. 15 on the ''Top Country Albums'' chart in 1985. In 1986, Charly and Wayne released a duet album ''When Love Is Right'' and the first single \"[[When It's Down to Me and You]]\" peaked at No. 17.\n\n==Later years==\nAfter 1986, McClain's success began to subside. Her 1987 ''Still I Stay'' album brought only one Top 40 single; \"[[Don't Touch Me There]]\" peaked at No. 20 on the Billboard Country Chart. The album became McClain's last album with [[Epic Records|Epic]]. Upon fulfilling her contract, she parted ways with the record label the following year. She continued to chart until her last recording came in 1989.<ref name=\"AMG\"/>   She recorded one studio album with [[Mercury Records]] before the end of the decade.<ref name=\"LarkinCountry\"/> Her last charted single was \"You Got the Job\", which peaked at No. 65. McClain has not recorded a studio album since 1988's self-titled album on Mercury Records.\n\n==Retirement and family==\nPreferring to spend more time with her husband and their families, McClain retired completely from touring, public appearances, and performances in the early 1990s. Later, she helped to care for her mother Virginia before she died in 2009.<ref name=\"Shackelford Funeral Directors\">{{Cite web|url=https://www.shackelfordfuneraldirectors.com/obituaries/Virginia-Jo-McClain-5820/|website=Shackelfordfuneraldirectors.com|title=Virginia Jo McClain Obituary|access-date=August 8, 2021}}</ref>\n\nCharly McClain and Wayne Massey have no children together. However, Massey does have a son from his first marriage.\n\nSeveral compilation albums of McClain's music have been released over the years. Probably the most noteworthy of these is 1999's ''Anthology.'' It included all of McClain's successful singles from her career with Epic. She continues to reside with her husband Wayne in the Memphis, Tennessee, area.\n\n==Discography==\n{{Main|Charly McClain discography}}\n\n== Awards and nominations ==\n{| (band)"}],"pages":{"45592498":{"pageid":45592498,"ns":0,"title":"Ward Thomas (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|English modern country-pop duo}}\n{{EngvarB|date=January 2018}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=January 2018}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name             = Ward Thomas\n| image            = \n| caption          = \n| landscape        = yes\n| origin           = [[Petersfield]],  [[Hampshire]], England\n| background       = group_or_band\n| alias            = \n| genre            = [[Country pop]], [[Americana (music)|Americana]]\n| years_active     = 2014\u2013present\n| label            = {{flatlist|\n*WTW Music\n*[[Sony Music]]}}\n| associated_acts  = \n| current_members  = * Catherine Ward Thomas\n* Lizzy Ward Thomas\n| past_members     = \n}}\n'''Ward Thomas''' are an English modern country-pop duo, composed of twin sisters Catherine and Lizzy Ward Thomas from [[Hampshire]].<ref name=\"Nott\">{{cite news |last=Wilson |first=Simon |url=http://www.nottinghampost.com/Ward-Thomas-play-Rescue-Rooms/story-25972833-detail/story.html |title=Country music stars Ward Thomas head for the Rescue Rooms |newspaper=[[Nottingham Post]] |date=4 February 2015 |accessdate=19 February 2016 |archive-date=10 July 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150710010347/http://www.nottinghampost.com/Ward-Thomas-play-Rescue-Rooms/story-25972833-detail/story.html |url-status=live }}</ref> The band has been called \"Britain's first country stars\".<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.thenorthernecho.co.uk/entertainment/11611066.Ward_Thomas_export_style_from_our_country_to_USA/?ref=rss |title=Ward Thomas export style from our country to USA |newspaper=[[The Northern Echo]] |date=19 November 2014 |accessdate=19 February 2016 |archive-date=2 March 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160302044054/http://www.thenorthernecho.co.uk/entertainment/11611066.Ward_Thomas_export_style_from_our_country_to_USA/?ref=rss |url-status=live }}</ref, their music has been described as written \"from a British perspective\". While people have been able to appreciate the American sound, they can connect with the themes of British lyrics.</ref> ''[[Cartwheels (Ward Thomas album)|Cartwheels]]'', their second studio album, became the first album by a UK country act to reach number one on the [[UK Albums Chart]]. surpassing the previous record by [[the Shires (duo)|the Shires]]. It has since gone gold in the UK.\n\n==Early life==\nCatherine and Lizzy are twins, born two minutes apart,<ref name=\"theguardian.com\">{{Cite web|url = https://www.theguardian.com/music/2016/sep/15/catherine-ward-thomas-mum-told-us-dont-swear-or-talk-politics-or-religion|title = Catherine Ward Thomas: 'Mum told us don't swear or talk politics or religion'|website = [[TheGuardian.com]]|date = 15 September 2016|access-date = 3 July 2020|archive-date = 3 July 2020|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20200703132926/https://www.theguardian.com/music/2016/sep/15/catherine-ward-thomas-mum-told-us-dont-swear-or-talk-politics-or-religion|url-status = live}}</ref> who grew up on a farm in rural Hampshire, England, and were educated at [[Alton School]], a [[Roman Catholic]] private day school, where they acquired the nicknames \"Scruff 1\" and \"Scruff 2\" because they were \"so bad at being neat and tidy\".<ref name=\"theguardian.com\"/>\n\nTheir father is Anthony Ward-Thomas, who in 1985 founded his own eponymous removals business, now with an annual turnover of \u00a322 million (2015).<ref>{{cite web |last1=Ward-Thomas |first1=Anthony |title=Who we are &#124; Anthony Ward Thomas &#124; UK and London Removals |url=https://ward-thomas.co.uk/who-we-are |access-date=21 February 2020 |archive-date=21 February 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200221083831/https://ward-thomas.co.uk/who-we-are |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://ward-thomas.co.uk/who-we-are|title=Who we are &#124; Anthony Ward Thomas &#124; UK and London Removals|access-date=21 February 2020|archive-date=21 February 2020|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200221083831/https://ward-thomas.co.uk/who-we-are|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>Natalie Graham, Financial Times, February 20, 2015, ''My First Million \u2014 Anthony Ward Thomas, A moving story of success from small beginnings''[https://www.ft.com/content/f11d7122-a545-11e4-ad35-00144feab7de] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200703113217/https://www.ft.com/content/f11d7122-a545-11e4-ad35-00144feab7de |date=3 July 2020 }}</ref> Their mother Amanda Ward Thomas is an artist.\n\n==Career==\n===2014\u20132015: ''From Where We Stand''===\n{{Main|From Where We Stand}}\nThey co-wrote the songs for their debut album ''[[From Where We Stand]]'', which was released on 20 July 2014. It peaked at number 41 on the [[UK Albums Chart]], number 1 on the UK Country Chart, number 7 on the [[UK Independent Singles and Albums Charts|UK Indie Chart]] and number 36 in [[Scottish Singles and Albums Charts|Scotland]]. The album won UK Album of the Year at the British Country Music Awards and sold over 25,000 copies.<ref name=\"Nott\"/> They have toured the UK multiple times, with shows at venues including [[Islington Assembly Hall]] and [[The New Adelphi Club]] in [[Kingston upon Hull|Hull]], [[East Riding of Yorkshire|East Yorkshire]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.facebook.com/events/1533175116949507/ |title=Under The Influence presents Ward Thomas |publisher=Facebook |accessdate=19 February 2016}}</ref>{{Primary source inline|date=January 2018}} In 2014, they performed on the [[BBC Introducing]] stage at the BBC Radio 2 Live in Hyde Park festival,<ref>{{cite web|title=Ward Thomas \u2013 Push For the Stride at Radio 2 Live in Hyde Park 2014|website=[[YouTube]]|date=15 September 2014|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=buEtZSwoevY|accessdate=12 June 2016|archive-date=16 October 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141016120031/https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=buEtZSwoevY&gl=US&hl=en|url-status=live}}</ref> returning to the festival in 2015 to perform on the main stage alongside The Shires; a performance which was broadcast live on [[BBC Radio 2]].<ref>{{cite web|title=The Shires & Ward Thomas \u2013 Everywhere (Radio 2 Live in Hyde Park 2015)|website=[[YouTube]]|date=13 September 2015|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7DzoDdxjHso|accessdate=12 June 2016|archive-date=16 September 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150916171733/https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7DzoDdxjHso&gl=US&hl=en|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n===2016\u20132017: ''Cartwheels'' and ''A Shorter Story''===\n{{Main|Cartwheels (Ward Thomas album)}}\nIn June 2016, Ward Thomas announced a joint venture with Sony Music and that their second album, ''[[Cartwheels (Ward Thomas album)|Cartwheels]]'', would be released in September 2016.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://twitter.com/wardthomasmusic/status/740643172330704896|title=Ward Thomas on Twitter|website=Twitter|access-date=12 June 2016}}</ref>{{Primary source inline|date=January 2018}} Lead single \"Carry You Home\", described by ''The Times'' as \"chirpy country pop\" was released in June, followed by the singles \"Guilty Flowers\" and \"Cartwheels\", all of which were added to the Radio 2 playlist. Cartwheels reached number 1 in the UK Albums Chart, making Ward Thomas the first UK country act to top the charts and officially making them the most successful UK country act. It has since gone gold in the UK.<ref>{{Cite news|title = Country duo Ward Thomas top UK album chart|work = BBC News|date = 9 September 2016|url = https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-37319660/|access-date = 21 June 2018|archive-date = 4 November 2018|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20181104021355/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-37319660|url-status = live}}</ref> In September 2016, Ward Thomas were confirmed to play at the 31st edition of [[Eurosonic Noorderslag]] in [[Groningen]]<ref>{{Cite web|title = First European Artists Confirmed for Eurosonic Noorderslag \u2013 Eurosonic Noorderslag|url = https://www.eurosonic-noorderslag.nl/en/news/festival/article/eerste-artiesten-voor-eurosonic-noorderslag-2017-bevestigd/|website = Eurosonic Noorderslag|accessdate = 11 October 2016|archive-date = 2 August 2017|archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20170802210425/https://www.eurosonic-noorderslag.nl/en/news/festival/article/eerste-artiesten-voor-eurosonic-noorderslag-2017-bevestigd/|url-status = live}}</ref> and in March 2017, Ward Thomas were announced as the official opening act for the [[C2C: Country to Country|Country to Country]] 2017 festival.\n\nOn 28 October 2016, Ward Thomas released the single version of \"Cartwheels\", featuring a cover of [[Lenny Kravitz]]'s song \"[[Fly Away (Lenny Kravitz song)|Fly Away]]\" which was also featured on the TV show \"[[Countrywise]]\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://celebmix.com/ward-thomas-release-lenny-kravitzs-fly-away-cover|title=Ward Thomas Release Lenny Kravitz's 'Fly Away' Cover|date=28 October 2016|publisher=|access-date=21 May 2017|archive-date=8 August 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170808074728/http://celebmix.com/ward-thomas-release-lenny-kravitzs-fly-away-cover/|url-status=live}}</ref> On 31 March 2017, Ward Thomas released their first EP, ''[[A Shorter Story]]'', which features the duo covering five of their favourite songs.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://itunes.apple.com/gb/album/a-shorter-story-ep/id1217842584|title=A Shorter Story - EP by Ward Thomas on Apple Music|website=[[iTunes]]|date=31 March 2017|publisher=|access-date=31 March 2017|archive-date=1 April 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170401060200/https://itunes.apple.com/gb/album/a-shorter-story-ep/id1217842584|url-status=live}}</ref> In 2017, they supported American country superstar [[Miranda Lambert]] on the UK leg of her [[Highway Vagabond Tour]].\n\n===2017\u2013present: ''Restless Minds''===\nIn July 2018, Ward Thomas announced that they will release their third album, ''[[Restless Minds]]''. The announcement coincided with the release of lead single \"Lie Like Me\", a biting indictment of lives faked online. During the 2019 [[C2C: Country to Country]] festival, the duo were surprised by [[Cam (singer)|Cam]] at the CMA Songwriter's Event with the [[Country Music Association Award for International Achievement|Jeff Walker Global Achievement Award]] from the [[Country Music Association]], making them only the second UK country act to receive the award.<ref>[https://bellesandgals.com/2019/03/07/ward-thomas-recieve-prestigious-cma-jeff-walker-global-artist-award/ Ward Thomas Receive Prestigious CMA Jeff Walker Global Artist Award] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191205200950/https://www.bellesandgals.com/2019/03/07/ward-thomas-recieve-prestigious-cma-jeff-walker-global-artist-award/ |date=5 December 2019 }}, Music News, March 7, 2019, by Laura Klonowski</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! scope=\"col\" rowspan=\"2\"| Title\n!
