and record producer}}\n{{About|the artist|the album|Hunter Hayes (album)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Hunter Hayes\n| background        = solo_singer\n| image             = Hayes in Memphis (cropped).jpg\n| caption           = Hayes performing in Memphis, TN in August 2019\n| birth_name        = Hunter Easton Hayes\n| birth_date        = {{birth date and age|1991|09|09}}\n| birth_place       = [[Breaux Bridge, Louisiana]], U.S.\n| genre             = {{hlist|[[Country pop]]|[[R&B]]|[[Blues music|blues]]|[[Pop music|pop]]|[[Country music|country]]|[[Cajun music|cajun]]|[[pop rock]]|[[alternative rock]]}}\n| years_active      = 1993\u2013present\n| occupation        = {{hlist|Singer|songwriter|record producer|multi-instrumentalist}}\n| instrument        = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar|piano|accordion}}\n| label             = {{hlist|[[Atlantic Records|Atlantic Nashville]]|[[Warner Music Nashville|Warner Nashville]]|LP Entertainment}}\n| associated_acts   = {{hlist|[[Lady A]]|[[Hunter Brothers]]}}\n| website           = {{URL|hunterhayes.com}}\n}}\n'''Hunter Easton Hayes''' (born September 9, 1991)<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.musicnewsnashville.com/hunter-hayes-celebrates-his-20th-birthday-at-house-of-blues|title=Hunter Hayes Celebrates His 20th Birthday at House of Blues|author=Dan Harr|work=Music News Nashville|date=September 14, 2011|access-date=September 14, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111110064648/http://www.musicnewsnashville.com/hunter-hayes-celebrates-his-20th-birthday-at-house-of-blues|archive-date=November 10, 2011|url-status=dead}}</ref> is an American multi-genre singer, songwriter, record producer, and multi-instrumentalist. He is proficient at more than 30 instruments.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/6077406/hunter-hayes-leads-country-youth-revolution-storyline-video-interview|title=Hunter Hayes Leads Country's Youth Revolution, Without a Pickup Truck or Beer in Sight|author=Deborah Evans Price|magazine=Billboard|date=May 6, 2014|access-date=May 6, 2014}}</ref>\n\nHayes released his [[Hunter Hayes (album)|self-titled debut album]] in 2011.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://tasteofcountry.com/hunter-hayes-debut-album/ |title=Hunter Hayes Sets Release Date for Debut Album |work=Taste of Country |date=August 24, 2011 |access-date=November 7, 2011 |first=Amanda |last=Hensel}}</ref> It reached number seven on the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]] and number one on the [[Top Country Albums]], and sold over 1.1 million copies. Its most successful single, \"[[Wanted (Hunter Hayes song)|Wanted]]\", sold over 3.5 million copies and made Hayes the youngest male act to ever top the [[Hot Country Songs|''Billboard'' Hot Country Songs]].\n\nHayes' commercial success and his talent both as a songwriter and instrumentalist prompted ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' to call him the leader of \"Country Music's Youth Revolution\" in 2014.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/6077406/hunter-hayes-leads-country-youth-revolution-storyline-video-interview |title=Hunter Hayes Leads Country's Youth Revolution, Without a Pickup Truck or Beer in Sight |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |date=May 6, 2014}}</ref> He has been nominated for five [[Grammy Award]]s including [[Grammy Award for Best New Artist|Best New Artist]], and won the 2012 [[CMA Award]] for [[Country Music Association Award for New Artist of the Year|New Artist of the Year]] and three [[Broadcast Music, Inc.|BMI Awards]].\n\n==Life and career==\nHayes was born on September 9, 1991, in [[Breaux Bridge, Louisiana]]; he is an only child.<ref>[http://www.hunterhayes.com/bio Hunter's Story] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120209104810/http://www.hunterhayes.com/bio |date=February 9, 2012 }}. HunterHayes.com. Retrieved on February 21, 2012.</ref> His parents both have [[Cajuns|Cajun]] ancestry, along with [[English people|English]], [[Scotch-Irish Americans|Scots-Irish]], and [[Germans|German]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.imdb.com/name/nm0371048/bio?ref_=nm_ov_bio_sm#trivia|title=Hunter Hayes : Biography|publisher=IMDb.com|access-date=May 10, 2014}}</ref> He grew up [[Catholic Church|Catholic]], singing songs in both English and French.<ref>{{cite journal |url=http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0,,20123577,00.html |title=Squeeze Play |journal=People |first=Jeremy |last=Helligar |date=October 27, 1997 |volume=48 |issue=17 |page=113 |access-date=May 2, 2013 |archive-date=April 21, 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140421054547/http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0,,20123577,00.html |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{Cite web |last=Wilkinson |first=Hannah |title=You Are Good Enough: Hunter Hayes and Jen Ledger Find Their Value In Christ |url=https://www.jesuscalling.com/podcast/good-enough-hunter-hayes-jen-ledger-find-value-christ/ |access-date=2022-08-14 |website=Jesus Calling |date=August 16, 2018 |language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nHayes started performing when he was 2. At 4, he began making appearances locally and on national television,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=iz0dAAAAIBAJ&pg=5100,573829&dq=hunter-hayes+accordion&hl=en|title=Kids keep Cajun traditions thriving|last=Rose|first=Christopher|date=April 4, 1997|work=The Tuscaloosa News|access-date=June 30, 2011}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/hunter-hayes-music-interview-2011/|title=Hunter Hayes Was 'Born' to Make Country Music|last=Conaway|first=Alanna|work=Taste of Country|date=June 13, 2011 |access-date=June 30, 2011}}</ref> including ''[[Maury (TV series)|Maury]]'', ''[[Rosie O'Donnell Show]]'', and the [[Nickelodeon]] game show ''[[Figure It Out]]'', where he performed \"[[Jambalaya (On the Bayou)]]\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mPpjNgdT2dk/ |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/youtube/20211219/mPpjNgdT2dk |archive-date=2021-12-19 |url-status=live|title=Hunter Hayes - \"Jambalaya\" on Figure it Out|website=[[YouTube]]|date=October 16, 2011 |access-date=August 1, 2012}}{{cbignore}}</ref> [[American Songwriter]] writes that \"Hayes received his first guitar from actor [[Robert Duvall]] at age 6\"<ref name=\"American Songwriter\">{{cite magazine|url=http://www.americansongwriter.com/2012/05/hunter-hayes-is-martin-guitars-latest-brand-ambassador/ |title=Hunter Hayes Is Martin Guitars' Latest Brand Ambassador |magazine=American Songwriter |author=Evan Schlansky |date=May 21, 2012 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130128022554/http://www.americansongwriter.com/2012/05/hunter-hayes-is-martin-guitars-latest-brand-ambassador/ |archive-date=January 28, 2013 |access-date=June 6, 2012 |df=mdy-all }}</ref> At age 7, he was invited to perform for President [[Bill Clinton]] for a [[White House]] lawn party. At 13, he appeared on [[America's Most Talented Kids]], a show hosted by [[Dave Coulier]]; he performed the hit [[Hank Williams]] song, \"[[Hey Good Lookin' (song)|Hey Good Lookin']]\". At age 9, Hunter released his debut independent studio album ''\"Through My Eyes\"'' on October 8, 2000, under Suagartown Records and Louisiana Red Hot Records.<ref>{{cite web|title=Through My Eyes - Hunter Hayes {{!}} Songs, Reviews, Credits {{!}} AllMusic|url=https://www.allmusic.com/album/through-my-eyes-mw0000053846|website=AllMusic|access-date=29 December 2017}}</ref> He released several more independent albums: ''Make a Wish'' in 2001, ''Holidays with Hunter'' in 2003, ''Honoring our French Heritage'' in 2006, and ''Songs About Nothing'' in 2008.\n\nIn 2008, he moved from Breaux Bridge to [[Nashville, Tennessee]], and signed with [[Universal Music Publishing Group]] as a songwriter. In 2010, Hayes co-wrote \"Play\" for the [[Rascal Flatts]] album ''[[Nothing Like This (album)|Nothing Like This]]''. In September, he was signed to [[Atlantic Records]] Nashville and began working on what would become his major-label debut.\n\nHayes appeared as the opening act of 10 dates of country star [[Taylor Swift]]'s [[Speak Now World Tour]] throughout the summer of 2011 and concluded his leg of the tour in St. Louis, Missouri.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.hunterhayes.com/news/hunter-hayes-will-open-taylor-swift-speak-now-north-american-tour-2011 |title=Hunter Hayes will open for Taylor Swift SPEAK NOW North American Tour 2011 |work=HunterHayes.com |date=March 4, 2011 |access-date=May 2, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120506142749/http://www.hunterhayes.com/news/hunter-hayes-will-open-taylor-swift-speak-now-north-american-tour-2011 |archive-date=May 6, 2012 |url-status=dead }}</ref> In April 2011, he went on his own radio tour where he debuted songs that would appear on his debut album.<ref name=\"radiotour\">{{cite web |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mpNAs08ZcVc  |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/youtube/20211219/mpNAs08ZcVc |archive-date=2021-12-19 |url-status=live|title=Hunter Hayes \u2013 Radio Tour (Week 1) |access-date=October 30, 2011 |author=Hunter Hayes |website=[[YouTube]] |date=April 2011}}{{cbignore}}</ref> His debut headlining tour was the Most Wanted Tour; the first leg of the tour began on October 8, 2011, in [[Beaumont, Texas]], and ended on December 4, 2011, in [[San Bernardino, California]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://tasteofcountry.com/hunter-hayes-2011-tour-dates/ |title=Hunter Hayes Sets Fall 2011 Tour Dates |work=Taste of Country |date=September 13, 2011 |access-date=November 7, 2011 |first=Alanna |last=Conaway}}</ref>\n\nHayes and singer [[Victoria Justice]] contributed a duet to the soundtrack of 2011's ''[[Footloose (2011 film)|Footloose]]'' remake, recording a cover of [[Mike Reno]]'s and [[Ann Wilson]]'s 1984 hit \"[[Almost Paradise (song)|Almost Paradise]]\" from the original film. From January to February 2012, Hayes was the opening act on the [[Rascal Flatts]] \"Thaw Out\" tour.<ref>[http://www.rascalflatts.com/story/news/rascal-flatts-announce-ithaw-out-2012i-tour Rascal Flatts Announce Thaw Out 2012 Tour]. RascalFlatts.com (October 17, 2011). Retrieved on February 21, 2012.</ref>\n[[File:Hunter Hayes.jpg|thumb|Hayes signing autographs in [[Frederick, Maryland]] in August 2012]]\n\n\"Where We Left Off\" is an original song, written by Hayes, that can be heard on the [[Act of Valor: The Album|soundtrack]] for the 2012 war film ''[[Act of Valor]]''.<ref>[http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/entertainment/53539733-81/act-valor-original-songs.html.csp 'Act of Valor' soundtrack features original songs from Lady Antebellum, more]. Sltrib.com (February 20, 2012). Retrieved on 2012-02-21.</ref>\n\nDuring the 2012 [[O Music Awards]], [[The Flaming Lips]] broke a [[Guinness World Record]] (previously held by [[Jay-Z]]) for most concerts played in multiple cities in a 24-hr. period. Hayes was the opening act for them at the Hattiesburg stop.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1688734/hunter-hayes-performs-on-o-music-awards.jhtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121105061428/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1688734/hunter-hayes-performs-on-o-music-awards.jhtml |url-status=dead |archive-date=November 5, 2012 |title=Hunter Hayes Performs on O Music Awards |work=[[Country Music Television]] |date=June 28, 2012 |access-date=May 2, 2013}}</ref>\n\nIn May 2012, [[Martin Guitars]] named Hayes as C.F. Martin & Co.'s newest brand ambassador. [[American Songwriter]] quoted Hayes on the subject: \"It is an absolute honor to be named an official Martin Ambassador and to be recognized by the Martin family.\"<ref name=\"American Songwriter\"/>\n\nOn September 7, 2012, he was inducted at the [[Mahalia Jackson Theater]] in [[New Orleans|New Orleans, Louisiana]], into the [[Louisiana Music Hall of Fame]].<ref>{{cite web |url=https://finance.yahoo.com/news/hunter-hayes-inducted-louisiana-music-194054387.html |title=Hunter Hayes Inducted Into Louisiana Music Hall of Fame |work=[[Yahoo! Finance]] |date=September 10, 2012 |access-date=May 2, 2013}}</ref>\n\n===2011\u20132014: ''Hunter Hayes'' and ''Storyline''===\n[[File:Hunter Hayes Gettysburg, PA.png|thumb|Hayes performing in 2013]]\n[[File:Five-time Grammy nominee Hunter Hayes performs his national anthem soundcheck, hours before Game 6 of the World Series. (30415750290).jpg|thumbnail|Hayes doing a soundcheck at [[Progressive Field]] in preparation for his performance of the [[Star Spangled Banner|US national anthem]] at Game 6 of the [[2016 World Series]]]]\n\nHayes's debut single, \"[[Storm Warning (song)|Storm Warning]]\", released to radio on May 16, 2011. His [[Hunter Hayes (album)|self-titled]] major-label debut album was released on October 11, 2011.<ref>[http://www.hunterhayes.com/news/hunter-hayes-release-self-titled-debut-album-atlantic-records-october-11 HUNTER HAYES TO RELEASE SELF-TITLED DEBUT ALBUM ON ATLANTIC RECORDS OCTOBER 11] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120220175525/http://www.hunterhayes.com/news/hunter-hayes-release-self-titled-debut-album-atlantic-records-october-11 |date=February 20, 2012 }}. HunterHayes.com (August 24, 2011). Retrieved on 2012-02-21.</ref> He co-wrote every song, played every instrument, and along with Dann Huff, produced the album.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=5319|title=Hunter Hayes becomes Next Big Thing|date=April 22, 2011|work=Country Standard Time|access-date=June 30, 2011}}</ref> \"[[Wanted (Hunter Hayes song)|Wanted]]\", the second single, was released to radio on March 5, 2012.\n\nOn July 24, 2012, he appeared on the CBS's ''The Talk'', where he was then given an RIAA Gold Certification plaque for \"Wanted\".<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.hunterhayes.com/news/hunters-interview-and-performance-talk |title=Hunter's Interview And Performance On The Talk |work=HunterHayes.com |date=July 25, 2012 |access-date=May 2, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121015165352/http://www.hunterhayes.com/news/hunters-interview-and-performance-talk |archive-date=October 15, 2012 |url-status=dead }}</ref> Just shy of two months since \"Wanted\" went gold, the song was certified Platinum by RIAA on August 23, 2012.\n\n\"Wanted\" became his first No. 1 single,<ref>{{cite web |url=http://tasteofcountry.com/hunter-hayes-wanted-no-1-single/ |title=Hunter Hayes Gets What He 'Wanted' With First No. 1 Single |work=Taste of Country |date=September 18, 2012 |first=Alanna |last=Conaway |access-date=May 2, 2013}}</ref> making him the youngest solo male act to top Hot Country Songs, breaking the record set in 1973 by [[Johnny Rodriguez]].<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/475001/hunter-hayes-makes-history-little-big-town-shines-on-country-charts |title=Hunter Hayes Makes History, Little Big Town Shines on Country Charts |magazine=Billboard |date=September 20, 2012 |first=Wade |last=Jessen |access-date=May 2, 2013}}</ref> Twenty weeks after first appearing in the top spot and under a new chart format, \"Wanted\" returned to the top spot.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/1539423/ask-billboard-whats-so-unusual-about-hunter-hayes-new-no-1/ |title=Ask Billboard: What's so unusual about Hunter Hayes's New No. 1 |magazine=Billboard |first=Gary |last=Trust |date=February 18, 2013 |access-date=May 2, 2013}}</ref> \"[[Somebody's Heartbreak]]\", the album's third single, went to No. 1 on the [[Country Airplay]] chart.<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Hunter Hayes Dupe 1 - Chart History (Country Airplay)|url= https://www.billboard.com/artist/hunter-hayes-dupe-1/chart-history/csa/ |magazine=Billboard|accessdate=February 11, 2023}}</ref>\n\nStarting September 14, 2012, Hayes began appearing as the opening act on 90+ dates for [[Carrie Underwood]]'s [[Blown Away Tour]].\n\nHe was also nominated for three Grammys including [[Grammy Award for Best New Artist|Best New Artist]] at the [[2013 Grammy Awards]]; he is the youngest male country artist to be nominated in all three categories for which he was nominated.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=http://www.billboardhcom/articles/columns/the-615/1538011/hunter-hayes-my-grammy-ritual |title=Hunter Hayes: My Grammy Ritual |magazine=Billboard |date=February 6, 2013 |first=Matt |last=Diehl |access-date=May 2, 2013 }}{{Dead link|date=January 2020 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=About Hunter Hayes|url=http://www.cmt.com/artists/hunter-hayes/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121220034549/http://www.cmt.com/artists/hunter-hayes/|url-status=dead|archive-date=December 20, 2012|access-date=March 16, 2013}}</ref> The album's fourth single, \"[[I Want Crazy]]\", which is from the deluxe ''Encore'' edition, was released to country radio on April 7, 2013. It peaked at number two on the Country Airplay chart in August 2013. Following it was \"[[Everybody's Got Somebody but Me]]\", a re-recording of a song from the original press of the album. The re-recorded version features guest vocals from [[Jason Mraz]].\n\nHunter was one of five country singers who won a CMT Artist of the Year award in 2013. This award is awarded every year to a group of country musicians who have had an outstanding year.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1718091/hunter-hayes-interview-cmt-artists-of-the-year.jhtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131130075801/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1718091/hunter-hayes-interview-cmt-artists-of-the-year.jhtml |url-status=dead |archive-date=November 30, 2013 |title=News : Hunter Hayes Interview: CMT Artists of the Year |publisher=CMT |date=November 28, 2013 |access-date=May 9, 2014}}</ref>\n\nHayes performed \"[[Invisible (Hunter Hayes song)|Invisible]]\", the lead single from his second album, at the [[56th Annual Grammy Awards]].<ref>{{cite web|author=Craig Shelburne |url=http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1721157/hunter-hayes-debuts-invisible-on-grammys.jhtml |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140129074928/http://www.cmt.com/news/country-music/1721157/hunter-hayes-debuts-invisible-on-grammys.jhtml |url-status=dead |archive-date=January 29, 2014 |title=News : Hunter Hayes Debuts \"Invisible\" on Grammys |publisher=CMT |date=January 26, 2014 |access-date=May 9, 2014}}</ref> ''[[Storyline (Hunter Hayes album)|Storyline]]'' was released on May 6, 2014.<ref name=\"news.radio.com\">{{cite web |url=http://news.radio.com/2014/03/11/hunter-hayes-new-album-storyline-to-drop-may-6/ |title=Hunter Hayes' New Album 'Storyline' to Drop May 6 \u00ab Radio.com |publisher=News.radio.com |date=March 11, 2014 |access-date=May 9, 2014 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140321031056/http://news.radio.com/2014/03/11/hunter-hayes-new-album-storyline-to-drop-may-6/ |archive-date=March 21, 2014 |url-status=dead }}</ref> In an effort to promote his album and to raise awareness to end child hunger, Hunter broke the Guinness World Record for the most concerts played in multiple cities in 24 hours, previously held by [[The Flaming Lips]].<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/6084729/hunter-hayes-breaks-the-flaming-lips-guinness-world-record-while-raising-awareness-most-concerts-played-in-multiple-cities-in-24-hours-conagra-Foods |title=Hunter Hayes Breaks Guinness World Record For Most Concerts Played in multiple cities in 24 hours |magazine=Billboard |date=May 10, 2014 |access-date=August 9, 2014}}</ref> The album's second single, \"[[Tattoo (Hunter Hayes song)|Tattoo]]\" released to country radio on June 16, 2014.\n\nOn July 20, 2014, Hayes's self-titled debut album was certified double platinum by the RIAA.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.riaa.com/gold-platinum/?tab_active=default-award&ar=Hunter+Hayes&ti=Hunter+Hayes#search_section|title=Gold & Platinum - RIAA|website=[[Recording Industry Association of America]]}}</ref> Following that was \"[[Light Me Up (Hunter Hayes song)|Light Me Up]]\", another single from the deluxe version of his debut album, in 2015.\n\n===2015\u20132018: ''The 21 Project'' and canceled album===\nOn May 21, 2015, Hayes released \"[[21 (Hunter Hayes song)|21]]\", which was the title track for both his EP and third studio album, [[The 21 Project]]. He also appeared on the track \"I Can Play Guitar\" on [[Brett Kissel]]'s album ''[[Pick Me Up (album)|Pick Me Up]]''.\n\nOn November 2, 2016, Hayes performed with four holograms of himself on Jimmy Kimmel Live's after the CMA show.\n\nIn March 2017, Hayes performed as part of the [[C2C: Country to Country]] festival in the UK where he played alongside [[Dan + Shay]] and [[Darius Rucker]] supporting [[Reba McEntire]] and would return in 2019 with [[Carly Pearce]] and [[Dustin Lynch]] in support of [[Lady A]]. Following \"21,\" Hayes released several songs including \u201c[[Yesterday's Song|Yesterday\u2019s Song]]\u201d which were slated to be part of a studio album set to be released in February 2018. Hayes then canceled the project citing \u201cshifted priorities.\u201d<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/8527354/hunter-hayes-wild-blue-interview|title=Hunter Hayes on His New Album, 'Wild Blue': 'What This Record Did for Me Was Something Pretty Profound'|first= Melinda |last=Newman |date= August 14, 2019 |magazine=Billboard }}</ref>\n\nHayes also appeared as a guest star in the Nickelodeon show ''Bella and the Bulldogs''.{{Citation needed|date=July 2019}}\n\n===2018\u2013present: ''Wild Blue'' and ''Red Sky''===\n{{see also|Red Sky (Hunter Hayes album) }}\nIn December 2018, Hayes guest starred on ''[[Darci Lynne]]: My Hometown Christmas''.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Delbel|first1=Julia|title=Star-Studded Lineup Revealed for 'Darci Lynne: A Hometown 2018|url-status=dead}}</ref> He also recorded a duet with Irish singer [[Catherine McGrath]] for her debut album ''[[Talk of This Town (album)|Talk of This Town]]''.\n\nIn January 2019, Hayes released his first radio single in three years titled \"Heartbreak\" which was the lead single for an upcoming album to be released by [[Warner Music Nashville]].<ref>{{cite web |title=Future Releases for It was the first country music awards program held by a major organization. The academy's signature \"hat\" trophy was created in 1968. The awards were first televised in 1972 on [[American Broadcasting Company|ABC]].\n\n{|class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! Year !! Category !! Nominated Work !! Result\n|-\n| rowspan=\"4\"|2013\n| New Male Vocalist of the Year<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://knue.com/a-look-at-the-acm-nominees-for-new-male-vocalist/|title=A Look At The ACM Nominees for New Male Vocalist|last=Reynolds|first=Leslie|website=101.5 KNUE|date=January 22, 2013 |access-date=2019-01-15}}</ref>\n| Hunter Hayes\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| Single Record of the Year<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/2013-acm-awards-winners/|title=2013 ACM Awards Winners \u2013 Full List|last=Staff|first=Taste of Country|website=Taste of Country|date=April 8, 2013 |access-date=2019-01-15}}</ref>\n| rowspan=\"3\"|\"[[Wanted (Hunter Hayes song)|Wanted]]\"\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| Song of the Year<ref name=\":0\" />\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| Video of the Year<ref name=\":0\" />\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n|}\n\n===American Country Awards===\nThe [[American Country Awards]] is a country music awards show, entirely voted on by fans. Created by the Fox Network, the awards honor country music artists in music, video, and touring categories. Hayes has won two awards from five nominations.\n\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n!Year\n!Category\n!Nominee / work\n!Result\n|-\n| rowspan=\"3\"| 2012\n| New Artist of the Year\n| Hunter Hayes\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| Single by a New Artist\n| rowspan=\"2\"|\"[[Wanted (Hunter Hayes song)|Wanted]]\"\n| {{won}}\n|-\n| Music Video by a New Artist\n| {{won}}\n|-\n|rowspan=\"2\"| 2013\n| Breakthrough Artist of the Year\n| Hunter Hayes\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| Single by a Breakthrough\n| \"Somebody's Heartbreak\"\n| {{nom}}\n|}\n\n===Grammy Awards===\nA [[Grammy Award]] (originally called '''Gramophone Award'''), or '''Grammy''', is an accolade by the [[National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences]] (NARAS) of the United States to recognize outstanding achievement in the [[music industry]]. The annual presentation ceremony features performances by prominent artists, and the presentation of those awards that have a more popular interest.\n\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n!Year\n!Category\n!Nominee / work\n!Result\n|-\n| rowspan=\"3\"|[[2013 Grammy Awards|2013]]\n| [[Grammy Award for Best New Artist|Best New Artist]]\n| Hunter Hayes\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[Grammy Award for Best Country Album|Best Country Album]]\n| ''Hunter Hayes''\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| rowspan=\"3\"|[[Grammy Award for Best Country Solo Performance|Best Country Solo Performance]]\n| \"[[Wanted (Hunter Hayes song)|Wanted]]\"\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[2014 Grammy Awards|2014]]\n| \"[[I Want Crazy]]\"\n| {{nom}}\n|-\n| [[2015 Grammy Awards|2015]]\n| \"[[Invisible (Hunter Hayes song)|Invisible]]\"\n| {{nom}}\n|}\n\n===Other awards===\n{| class=\"wikitable\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Caitlyn_Smith","to":"Caitlyn Smith"}],"pages":{"54192584":{"pageid":54192584,"ns":0,"title":"Caitlyn Smith","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=December 2022}}\n{{Short description|American singer-songwriter and musician (born 1986)}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Caitlyn Smith\n| image =\n| caption = Smith performing at the [[C2C: Country to Country]] festival in 2022\n| birth_name = Caitlyn Elizabeth Smith\n| birth_date = {{birth date and age|1986|06|13}}\n| birth_place = [[Cannon Falls, Minnesota]], U.S.<ref name=\"allmusic\">{{cite web | url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/caitlyn-smith-mn0000438452/biography | title=Caitlyn Smith biography | publisher=AllMusic | accessdate=March 9, 2021}}</ref>\n| origin = [[Nashville, Tennessee]], U.S.\n| genre = [[Country Pop]]<ref name=\"allmusic\"/>\n| occupation = {{hlist|Singer|Songwriter}}\n| label = [[Monument Records|Monument]]\n| website = {{url|caitlynsmith.com}}\n}}\n'''Caitlyn Elizabeth Smith'''<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.ascap.com/es/repertory#/ace/search/workID/883477058?page=1 |title=THE HEART OF DIXIE |website=ASCAP |publisher=American Society of Composers, Authors and Publishers |access-date=September 19, 2023}}</ref> (born June 13, 1986) is an American singer-songwriter and musician. She was raised in [[Cannon Falls, Minnesota]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.elle.com/culture/music/a44994/caitlyn-smith-profile/|title=How Caitlyn Smith Defied Sex Symbol Clich\u00e9s to Break Out in Nashville|date=May 2, 2017|work=ELLE|access-date=July 11, 2017|language=en}}</ref> Smith's debut album ''[[Starfire (Caitlyn Smith album)|Starfire]]'' was released on Monument Records on January 19, 2018.<ref name=\"auto\">{{Cite magazine|title= Caitlyn Smith Steps Into the Spotlight With 'Starfire' After Penning Songs for Meghan Trainor and Garth Brooks|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/8070989/caitlyn-smith-starfire-premiere|access-date=December 19, 2017}}</ref> Her second studio album, ''Supernova'', was released on March 13, 2020.<ref name=\"supernova\"/> Her third album ''[[High & Low (Caitlyn Smith album)|High & Low]]'' was released on April 14, 2023.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Toth|first1=Emma|title=Caitlyn Smith To Release Self-Produced Third Album, 'High & Low'|url=https://countrynow.com/caitlyn-smith-to-release-self-produced-third-album-high-low/|website=Country Now|access-date=April 13, 2023|date=January 25, 2023}}</ref>\n\nShe has written songs recorded by [[Meghan Trainor]] (\"[[Like I'm Gonna Lose You]]\", duet with [[John Legend]], #1 on [[Adult Top 40|Billboard Adult Top 40]] chart), [[Kenny Rogers]] and [[Dolly Parton]] (\"[[You Can't Make Old Friends]]\"), [[Avicii]]  (\"Chained\") and (\"Love\"), [[Miley Cyrus]] (\"High\") and more.\n\nShe released the EP ''Starfire'' in July 2016. In January 2017, she announced she had signed a label deal with the newly reformed [[Monument Records]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Sony Music's Monument Records Revived By Jason Owen, Shane McAnally|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/business/7669714/monument-records-sony-music-label|website=Billboard.com|accessdate=July 11, 2017}}</ref> Smith has played at [[Lollapalooza]], Bourbon & Beyond Festival, Americana Fest and ACL Fest.<ref name=\"auto\"/>\n\nCaitlyn was named one of [[Rolling Stone Magazine]]'s \"10 New Artists You Need To Know\".<ref>{{cite web|title=10 New Country Artists You Need To Know: May 2016| date=May 4, 2016 |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/10-new-country-artists-you-need-to-know-may-2016-20160504/caitlyn-smith-20160504|publisher=Rolling Stone Country|accessdate=July 11, 2017}}</ref> She recorded \"The Card You Gamble\", the theme song of the drama series ''[[Monarch (American TV series)|Monarch]]'', which premiered in 2022.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://entertainment-focus.com/2022/01/14/listen-caitlyn-smith-unveils-the-card-you-gamble-the-theme-from-monarch/ | title=Listen: Caitlyn Smith unveils 'The Card You Gamble', the theme from 'Monarch' | date=January 14, 2022 }}</ref>\n\n== Personal life ==\nCaitlyn lives in Nashville with her husband, songwriter Rollie Gaalswyk. They have three sons together, Thomas Miles Gaalswyk (born in 2016), Lewis James Gaalswyk (born in 2018), and Jacob Roland Gaalswyk (born in 2023).<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://people.com/parents/caitlyn-smith-welcomes-son-lewis-james/|title=Her New Little 'Starfire' Has Arrived! Caitlyn Smith Introduces Son Lewis James: 'So Grateful'|website=People.com}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://celebritybabies.people.com/2016/09/12/caitlyn-smith-welcomes-son-thomas-miles/|title=Caitlyn Smith Welcomes Son Thomas Miles|website=People.com|access-date=July 12, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.instagram.com/p/C0PGvfOsxX6/?img_index=1|title=Welcome to the world, JACOB ROLAND GAALSWYK!|website=Instagram.com}}</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n=== Studio Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Chase_Rice","to":"Chase Rice"}],"pages":{"38077204":{"pageid":38077204,"ns":0,"title":"Chase Rice","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer-songwriter and football player}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2019}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Chase Rice\n| image           = Chase Rice - cropped.jpg\n| caption         = Rice in 2016\n| birth_name      =\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1985|9|19}}<br>[[Ormond Beach, Florida]]\n| origin          = [[Asheville, North Carolina]], U.S.\n| instrument      = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar}}\n| genre           = {{hlist|[[Country pop]]|[[country rock]]}}\n| occupation      = {{hlist|Singer|songwriter}}\n| years_active    = 2010\u2013present\n| label           = {{hlist|Dack Janiels|[[Sony Music Nashville|Columbia Nashville]]|[[BBR Music Group|BBR]]}}\n| website         = {{URL|chaserice.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Chase Rice''' (born September 19, 1985<ref>{{cite news|last1=Casey|first1=Jim|title=Chase Rice Might talk New Single, Wikipedia Errors and Showing More \"Depth\" With an Upcoming Album|url=http://www.nashcountrydaily.com/2016/07/01/chase-rice-talks-new-single-wikipedia-errors-and-showing-more-depth-with-upcoming-album/|access-date=July 2, 2016|work=Nash Country Daily|date=July 1, 2016}}</ref>) is an American [[country music]] singer, songwriter and reality television personality. He first came to prominence in 2010 while he was a contestant on ''[[Survivor: Nicaragua]]'', where he was the runner-up to [[Jud Birza|Jud \"Fabio\" Birza]]. In the same year Rice began focusing on a career in country music, and later co-wrote the diamond-certified single \"[[Cruise (song)|Cruise]]\", performed by [[Florida Georgia Line]].\n\nRice has released six studio albums, and his third album, ''[[Ignite the Night]]'', debuted atop the ''Billboard'' [[Top Country Albums]] chart.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/6236407/chase-rice-country-albums-number-one|title=Chase Rice|date=August 28, 2014|magazine=Billboard|access-date=October 21, 2014}}</ref> He has also scored two number-one singles on the [[Country Airplay]] chart with \"[[Eyes on You (Chase Rice song)|Eyes on You]]\"<ref>{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/8510439/chase-rice-eyes-on-you-no-1-country-airplay|title=Chase Rice Lands First Country Airplay No. 1 With 'Eyes On You'|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2019-08-28}}</ref> and \"[[Drinkin' Beer. Talkin' God. Amen.]]\" (featuring Florida Georgia Line). Prior to 2010, Rice was a former [[college football]] [[linebacker]] for the [[North Carolina Tar Heels football|North Carolina Tar Heels]] and a former [[NASCAR]] [[pit crew]] member for [[Hendrick Motorsports]].\n\n==Early life, education, and early career==\nBorn in Florida, Rice was raised on a farm in [[Asheville, North Carolina]]. He attended [[AC Reynolds High School]]<ref name=\"Chase Rice Biography\">{{cite web|title=Chase Rice Biography|url=http://www.gactv.com/gac/ar_artists_a-z/article/0,,GAC_26071_6037395,00.html|archive-url=https://archive.today/20130124135747/http://www.gactv.com/gac/ar_artists_a-z/article/0,,GAC_26071_6037395,00.html|url-status=dead|archive-date=January 24, 2013|work=Artists|publisher=Great American Country}}</ref> and the [[University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill]] where he was a linebacker on the [[North Carolina Tar Heels football|football team]]. He did not pursue an [[National Football League|NFL]] career due to injury.<ref name=\"Debuts Big\">{{cite news|last=Dauphin|first=Chuck|title=Spotlight: Ex-'Survivor' Star Chase Rice Debuts Big With 'Dirt Road Communion'|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/488389/spotlight-ex-survivor-star-chase-rice-debuts-big-with-dirt-road|newspaper=Billboard|date=May 16, 2012}}</ref><ref name=\"ocregister-concert-preview\">{{cite news|last1=Fadorski|first1=Kelli Skye|title=From a NASCAR pit crew member to 'Survivor' star, Chase Rice still prefers country music|url=http://www.ocregister.com/articles/rice-745140-country-really.html|access-date=February 28, 2017|work=[[Orange County Register]]|date=February 28, 2017}}</ref>\n\nAfter graduating from UNC, Rice was selected to join the [[Hendrick Motorsports]] [[pit crew]] as the rear tire carrier for [[Ryan Newman (racing driver)|Ryan Newman]]'s [[Nationwide Series]] car. He also worked on [[Jimmie Johnson]]'s [[Sprint Cup Series]] car and won two championships with the [[Lowe's]] team.<ref name=\"Chase Rice Biography\"/><ref name=\"Rice Hill Country\">{{cite web|title=Chase Rice|url=http://hillcountry.com/dc/music-calendar/single-event/189543/|publisher=Hill Country BBQ, Washington, D.C.|access-date=March 5, 2016}}{{Dead link|date=July 2020 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref>\n\n==''Survivor''==\nRice was selected as a cast member of the [[reality television]] show ''[[Survivor: Nicaragua]]''. He said that he was able to get his application into [[CBS]] through a college friend who had a connection with the network.<ref name=\"runner-up talks\">{{cite news|title=Exclusive: 'Survivor: Nicaragua' runner-up Chase Rice talks|url=http://www.realitytvworld.com/news/exclusive-survivor-nicaragua-runner-up-chase-rice-talks-11830.php|newspaper=Reality TV World|date=December 22, 2012}}</ref>\n\nRice was originally on the La Flor tribe, consisting of younger contestants. During his time on the tribe, he was quickly attracted to fellow contestant Brenda Lowe, who became aware of his attraction and used it to her advantage, recruiting him and several others into an alliance. After La Flor won three of the first four tribal immunity challenges, the tribes were blended and Rice ended up on the new version of the original \"older contestants\" tribe, Espada, while Lowe remained on the new version of the La Flor tribe. Rice and Lowe both ultimately made it to the merged group, Libertad, where their alliance successfully caused the eliminations of Alina Wilson and Marty Piombo, before turning on Lowe and eliminating her as a threat. Following Lowe's elimination, Rice continued with the alliance under new leader Matthew \"Sash\" Lenahan. After two contestants (NaOnka Mixon and \"Purple Kelly\" Shinn) quit, the alliance continued eliminating targets Ben \"Benry\" Henry, Jane Bright, Dan Lembo, and Holly Hoffman, although Bright and Hoffman were members of the alliance. The alliance tried to eliminate [[Jud Birza|Jud \"Fabio\" Birza]] as a threat against the jury, but Birza managed to evade them by winning the last three immunity challenges. Rice performed exceptionally well in the post-merge challenges, being on the winning team in two of the three team-oriented rewards, and winning the last two individual rewards. Eventually, Rice made it to the final three with Lenahan and Birza, where he had a chance to win the $1 million as \"Sole Survivor\". In pleading his case to the jury, Rice claimed that he was being open about how he played the game, but was criticized both for his rash decisions and occasional indecisiveness, as well as being perceived as a follower under both Lowe and Lenahan. Although both Rice and Lenahan tried to accuse Birza of not knowing what was going on in the competition, the jury still ultimately chose Birza who received five of the nine votes; Rice received the votes of Hoffman, Bright, Lowe, and Wilson.\n\nOn the nationally televised reunion show, Rice played his single \"Buzz Back\".<ref name=\"Country Song on Season Finale\">{{cite web|last=Wilkening|first=Matthew|title='Survivor' Finalist Chase Rice Debuts Country Song on Season Finale|date=December 20, 2010 |url=http://tasteofcountry.com/survivor-finalist-chase-rice-country-song-season-finale/|publisher=Taste of Country}}</ref> Although he received national media attention on the show, he says that reality show stardom did not help propel his country music career; instead, he cited it as an important life event that was more valuable than money and that put his life in perspective.\n\nIn the official issue of ''[[CBS Watch]]'' magazine, commemorating the 15th anniversary of ''[[Survivor (TV series)|Survivor]]'' in 2015, Rice was voted by viewers as the 10th \"steamiest\" male contestant in ''Survivor'' history.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://twitter.com/DaltonRoss/status/565168330513080320 |title=Wait, where's @JohnMCochran? |publisher=Twitter |first=Dalton |last=Ross |date=February 10, 2015 |access-date=February 10, 2015}}</ref>\n\n==Country music career==\n[[File:Chase Rice Mojo Club 2020.jpg|thumb|right|175px|Rice in 2020]]\nChase Rice began playing guitar in college. He cites his father as the inspiration for his career, recalling his father saying \"boy anyone can play guitar, but no one is gonna really listen to you until you start singing.\"<ref name=\"Rice Hill Country\"/> He creates his albums based on the live shows he has and is building his career through performing.<ref name=\"Debuts Big\"/> His first studio album, ''Friday Nights & Sunday Mornings'', was released on April 22, 2010. This 13-track album includes the first song he ever wrote/recorded, \"Larger Than Life\", which is about the passing of his father. This is the only full-length album Rice has released that is not available for digital purchase or streaming.\n\nIn March 2011, he released ''Country as Me'', a six-track EP featuring his single \"Buzz Back\". He has received air play as a \"Highway Find\" on satellite radio channel [[The Highway (Sirius XM)|The Highway]]. In April 2012, his second studio album ''[[Dirt Road Communion]]'' debuted at number 48 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Billboard charts|Country Albums]] chart.<ref name=\"Debuts Big\" /> This album included the original recordings of \"Jack Daniels and Jesus\" and \"How She Rolls\", the latter of which has been removed from streaming and digital platforms in its original form. \"Whoa\" has also been removed from all digital and streaming platforms, but was never re-released leaving the current total tracks on the album at 14. \"Happy Hour (Worktape)\" includes a hidden track, \"Kiss My Ass\", which begins at the 4:31 minute mark on the song.\n\nIn July 2012, he signed with [[Creative Artists Agency]].<ref name=\"Signs with CAA\">{{cite news|title=Indie artist Chase Rice Signs with CAA|url=http://nashvillecountryclub.com/News.php?id=4177|newspaper=Nashville Country Club|date=July 19, 2012|access-date=December 31, 2012|archive-date=January 3, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190103005104/http://nashvillecountryclub.com/News.php?id=4177|url-status=dead}}</ref> He was a co-writer of [[Florida Georgia Line]]'s \"[[Cruise (song)|Cruise]]\" which topped ''Billboard'' [[Hot Country Songs]].<ref name=\"Platinum Success\">{{cite web|title=Chase Rice 'Cruise's with Florida Georgia Line to Platinum Success and a #1 Single|url=http://www.gotcountryonline.com/chase-rice-cruises-with-florida-georgia-line-to-platinum-success-and-a-1-single/|publisher=Got Country Online|access-date=December 28, 2012}}</ref>\n\nIn October 2013, he released ''[[Ready Set Roll (EP)|Ready Set Roll]]'', a six-song EP including the title track. The physical version of the album was released in November 2013 and included the bonus song \"Jack Daniel's and Jesus\". On January 29, 2014, the official \"[[Ready Set Roll]]\" music video premiered exclusively on CMT.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://chaserice.com/103-official-ready-set-roll-music-video-premieres-on-cmt|title=Official Ready Set Roll Music Video Premieres on CMT |access-date=February 4, 2016 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140221113825/http://chaserice.com/103-official-ready-set-roll-music-video-premieres-on-cmt |archive-date=February 21, 2014 }}</ref> The next day the video debuted on VEVO. He partnered with [[Columbia Records]] for distribution of \"Ready Set Roll\" in March 2014.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.musicrow.com/2014/03/columbia-nashville-inks-strategic-partnership-with-chase-rice/|title=Columbia Nashville Inks Strategic Partnership With Chase Rice|work=MusicRow - Nashville's Music Industry Publication - News, Songs From Music City|date=March 27, 2014 |access-date=October 21, 2014}}</ref>\n\nOn June 30, 2014, Rice released the album cover, release date, and album sequence for ''[[Ignite the Night]]''. The full-length album was released on August 19, 2014, and included the platinum-certified single, \"Ready Set Roll\".\n\nIn February 2016, Rice released \"Whisper\", which was intended to be the lead single from an upcoming album. The song was unsuccessful commercially, peaking at number 56 on the week of April 23, 2016, after just 3 weeks of being on the Country Airplay chart.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=http://www.billboard.com/artist/299025/chase-rice/chart?f=1226 |title=Chase Rice - Chart history |magazine=Billboard |access-date=July 31, 2016}}</ref> It is currently the single which has peaked the lowest for Rice only behind \"How She Rolls\" which peaked at number 55 in 2013, and never received real label backing. After releasing the single, Rice issued a letter to his fans which said, \"If you have listened to my music for years and want to hear more depth and meaning, I very much appreciate you, too, and your desires will also be fulfilled on this album (and truthfully, that was my goal on previous albums with songs like \"Carolina Can\" and \"Every Song I Sing\").\" He went on to mention that he was influenced by [[Garth Brooks]] and [[Kenny Chesney]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://countrymusicrocks.net/2016/02/chase-rice-pens-honest-and-heartfelt-letter-to-fans.html/|title=Chase Rice Pens Honest and Heartfelt Letter to Fans|date=February 5, 2016|website=Country Music Rocks|language=en-US|access-date=December 1, 2021}}</ref> Rice then released \"Everybody We Know Does\", which was sent to country radio on June 24, 2016.<ref>{{cite web|author=Lauren Laffer|url=http://www.soundslikenashville.com/music/chase-rice-releases-new-single-everybody-we-know-does/ |title=Chase Rice Releases New Single, 'Everybody We Know Does' Sounds Like Nashville |publisher=Soundslikenashville.com |date=June 24, 2016 |access-date=July 31, 2016}}</ref>\n\nAfter \"Everybody We Know Does\" failed to crack the top 25, Rice left Columbia in 2017 and signed to [[BBR Music Group|Broken Bow Records]] the same year. The lead single from Rice's first album with BBR, \"Three Chords and the Truth\", was sent to country radio.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/chase-rice-bbr-music-group-broken-bow-records/|title=Chase Rice Signs With Broken Bow, Ready to Release New Music|website=The Boot|date=June 21, 2017 |access-date=December 10, 2017}}</ref> This single was highly praised by both country fans and radio, as this was his first single to crack the Top 25 on the [[Country Airplay]] chart in 4 years. ''Lambs & Lions'' is Rice's first album on Broken Bow Records/BMG and is also the first album released by BBR since the BMG takeover. The album was released on November 17, 2017.\n\nRice's single \"[[Eyes on You (Chase Rice song)|Eyes on You]]\" became his first number one on country radio on May 6, 2019, staying at the top for two weeks.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Stevens |first1=Buck |title=Chase Rice Holds Number One for Second Week with \"Eyes On You\" |url=http://www.wbwn.com/2019/05/13/chase-rice-holds-number-one-for-second-week-with-eyes-on-you/ |website=wbwn.com |date=May 13, 2019 |access-date=23 May 2019}}</ref> He then released the follow-up single \"[[Lonely If You Are]]\" on July 1, 2019.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.thecountrydaily.com/2019/06/07/chase-rice-drops-friendly-new-single-lonely-if-you-are-listen/ | title=Chase Rice Drops Friendly New Single, \"Lonely If You Are\" [Listen] | publisher=The Country Daily | date=June 7, 2019 | access-date=September 22, 2020 | author=Jim Casey}}</ref> Rice also wrote and performed the inaugural theme song for ''[[The Pat McAfee Show]]'', which was used from September 10, 2019, to April 30, 2020.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ie1pN5HscGk|title=The Pat McAfee Show - Tuesday September 10th|date=September 10, 2019|via=YouTube}}<br>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=xxZCaGmkDTI|title=The Pat McAfee Show - Thursday, April 30th|date=April 30, 2020|via=YouTube}}</ref>\n\nRice appeared on the fourth episode of [[The Bachelor (season 24)|season 24 of ''The Bachelor'']], performing at a private concert for bachelor [[Peter Weber (television personality)|Peter Weber]] and his date, Victoria Fuller, at [[Cedar Point]] in [[Sandusky, Ohio]]. Fuller later revealed that she had previously dated Rice.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/entertainment/tv/2020/01/27/the-bachelor-chase-rice-claims-he-didnt-expect-perform-ex/4594060002/|title=Singer Chase Rice expresses frustration over the 'drama' he was dragged into on 'The Bachelor'|last=Trepany|first=Charles|website=USA TODAY|language=en-US|access-date=2020-01-29}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cnn.com/2020/01/28/entertainment/chase-rice-bachelor-trnd/index.html|title=Chase Rice claims 'Bachelor' producers blindsided him with his ex-girlfriend on latest episode|first=Marianne |last=Garvey|website=CNN|date=January 28, 2020 |access-date=2020-01-29}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cleveland.com/entertainment/2020/01/cedar-point-episode-of-the-bachelor-was-a-cold-blustery-lesson-in-reality-and-it-wasnt-pretty.html|title=Cedar Point episode of 'The Bachelor' was a cold, blustery lesson in reality . . . and it wasn't pretty|first=Chuck|last=Yarborough|work=The Plain Dealer|date=2020-01-27|language=en|access-date=2020-01-29}}</ref>\n\nOn June 27, 2020, Rice played a concert at the [[Brushy Mountain State Penitentiary]], in [[Petros, Tennessee]], where many fans chose to ignore recommended safety measures against spreading and contracting [[COVID-19]]. Reaction to the concert drew negative outcry from fans and the music industry.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-06-29|title=As COVID-19 surges, country star Chase Rice plays packed concert for a thousand mask-free fans|url=https://www.latimes.com/entertainment-arts/music/story/2020-06-28/chase-rice-country-concert-covid-19|access-date=2020-06-29|website=Los Angeles Times|language=en-US}}</ref> In response to the criticism Rice stated: \"If it were up to me I wouldn't cancel one damn show, but it ain't.... I personally, choose not to live scared, especially of something that I can't really control.\"<ref>{{Cite news|date=2020-06-30|title=Country singers criticize Chase Rice as 'selfish' for concert in front of hundreds in Tennessee|newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/arts-entertainment/2020/06/29/chase-rice-concert-social-distancing-tennessee/#comments-wrapper|language=en-US}}</ref>\n\nIn November 2020, Rice released the single \"[[Drinkin' Beer. Talkin' God. Amen.]]\" featuring his long-time friends Florida Georgia Line.<ref>{{cite web | url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/pamwindsor/2020/11/30/chase-rice-teams-up-with-florida-georgia-line-for-new-song-drinkin-beer-talkin-god-amen/?sh=60409295c39e| title=Chase Rice Teams Up With Florida Georgia Line For New Song 'Drinkin' Beer Talkin' God Amen'| work=[[Forbes]]| date=November 30, 2020| access-date=December 4, 2020 |first=Pam|last=Windsor}}</ref> It is the second single from Rice's fifth studio album, ''[[The Album (Chase Rice album)|The Album]]'', which was released on May 28, 2021.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.allaccess.com/country/future-releases|title=Future Releases for Country Radio Stations|accessdate=May 29, 2021|work=AllAccess}}</ref>\n\nIn November 2022, Rice announced his sixth studio album ''I Hate Cowboys & All Dogs Go to Hell'', which was released in February 2023.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.wfms.com/news/chase-rice-announces-new-album-i-hate-cowboys-all-dogs-go-to-hell/|title=Chase Rice Announces New Album 'I Hate Cowboys & All Dogs Go To Hell'|website=[[WFMS]]|date=November 20, 2022|access-date=February 9, 2023|archive-date=November 21, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221121045120/https://www.wfms.com/news/chase-rice-announces-new-album-i-hate-cowboys-all-dogs-go-to-hell/|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/chase-rice-album-interview-i-hate-cowboys-1235251656/|title=Chase Rice Finds His True Voice On New Album 'I Hate Cowboys & All Dogs Go to Hell'|work=Forbes|first=Pam|last=Windsor|date=February 20, 2023|access-date=October 24, 2023}}</ref> The sole single from the album, \"Bad Day to Be a Cold Beer\",<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bbrmusicgroup.com/chase-rice-delivers-summer-anthem-bad-day-cold-beer-country-radio/|title=CHASE RICE DELIVERS SUMMER ANTHEM \"BAD DAY TO BE A COLD BEER\" TO COUNTRY RADIO|website=bbrmusicgroup.com|date=May 8, 2023|access-date=October 24, 2023}}</ref> was released in May and music videos were produced for \"Bench Seat\", \"Way Down Yonder\" and \"I Hate Cowboys\".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.billboard.com/music/country/chase-rice-album-interview-i-hate-cowboys-1235251656/|title=Chase Rice Refines His Artistic Voice on New Album: 'I'm Not Chasing Anything Anymore'|work=Billboard|first=Jessica|last=Nicholson|date=February 10, 2023|access-date=October 24, 2023}}</ref> During the year, Rice promoted the album on the Way Down Yonder tour,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/chase-rice-2023-way-down-yonder-tour-dates/|title=Chase Rice Will Showcase New Album on 2023 Way Down Yonder Tour|work=Taste of Country|author=Jess|date=December 13, 2022|access-date=October 24, 2023}}</ref> and was a supporting act for [[Jelly Roll (singer)|Jelly Roll]] and [[Old Dominion (band)|Old Dominion]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://countrynow.com/jelly-roll-facetimes-ashley-mcbryde-chase-rice-more-to-make-big-announcement/|title=Jelly Roll FaceTimes Ashley McBryde, Chase Rice & More To Make Big Announcement|work=Country Now|first=Lauren Jo|last=Black|date=February 20, 2023|access-date=October 24, 2023}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://countrynow.com/old-dominion-extends-no-bad-vibes-tour-with-new-arena-shows-and-special-guests/|title=Old Dominion Extends No Bad Vibes Tour With New Arena Shows And Special Guests|work=Country Now|first=Madeleine|last=O'Connell|date=May 2, 2023|access-date=October 24, 2023}}</ref> In early 2024, Rice will embark on his headlining \"Get Western Tour\" across Canada and the [[Pacific Northwest]], with [[Owen Riegling]] and Palmer Anthony as supporting acts.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicrow.com/2023/11/chase-rice-to-head-up-north-for-get-western-tour/|title=Chase Rice To Head Up North For \u2018Get Western Tour\u2019|date=November 22, 2023|first=Lorie|last=Hollabaugh|work=Music Row|access-date=December 25, 2023}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{main|Chase Rice Yonder Tour (2023)\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* [http://www.cbs.com/shows/survivor/cast/44279/ Chase Rice biography] for ''[[Survivor: Nicaragua]]'' at [[CBS]].com\n*
