Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Cam_(singer)","to":"Cam (singer)"}],"pages":{"47078839":{"pageid":47078839,"ns":0,"title":"Cam (singer)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American country music singer and songwriter}}\n{{good article}}\n{{Infobox person\n| name               = Cam\n| image              = Country singer Cam at Bra Country Concert.jpg\n| caption            = Cam performing live in 2015\n| birth_name         = Camaron Marvel Ochs<ref name=\"burning\">{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/hear-cams-haunting-new-single-burning-house-20150618|title=Hear Cam's Haunting New Hit Single 'Burning House'|last=Shelburne|first=Craig|date=18 June 2015|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=25 June 2015}}</ref>\n| birth_date         = {{birth date and age|1984|11|19}}<ref name=\"Allmusic Bio\"/>\n| birth_place        = [[Huntington Beach, California]], U.S.\n| education          = [[University of California, Davis]]\n| other_names        = <!--Per Template:Infobox person and MOS:MULTINAMES, it is not necessary to list off her names here. Also see WP:BLP.-->\n| occupation         = {{flat list|\n* Singer\n* songwriter\n}}\n| years_active       = 2010\u2013present\n| spouse             = {{marriage|Adam Weaver<br />|2016}}\n| children           = 1\n| awards             = \n| website            = \n| module             = {{Infobox musical artist\n| embed           = yes\n| genre           = [[Country pop]]\n| instrument      = Vocals\n| label           = {{flat list|\n*Rubber Room\n*[[Arista Nashville]]\n*[[RCA Records|RCA]]/[[Thirty Tigers]]\n}}\n| website         = [http://www.camcountry.com/ camcountry.com]\n}}\n}}\n'''Camaron Marvel Ochs''' (born November 19, 1984), known professionally as '''Cam''', is an American [[country music]] singer and songwriter. She began her career as a songwriter and has composed material for several artists including [[Beyonc\u00e9]], [[Sam Smith (singer)|Sam Smith]] and [[Miley Cyrus]]. In 2010, she released her debut studio album ''Heartforward'' on an independent record label. Signing with [[Sony Music Entertainment]], she released her debut major label [[extended play|EP]] in March 2015, ''[[Welcome to Cam Country]]'', followed by the studio album ''[[Untamed (Cam album)|Untamed]]'' later that same year. Her third album was ''[[The Otherside (album)|The Otherside]]'', released on [[Thirty Tigers|Triple Tigers]] in 2020. Her second single \"[[Burning House]]\" is her most commercially successful, peaking at the number two position on ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] and [[Country Airplay]]. Spurred by airplay on ''[[The Bobby Bones Show]]'', the song received widespread acclaim, including a Best Country Solo Performance nomination at the [[58th Annual Grammy Awards]] and a Triple Platinum certification by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]] (RIAA).\n\n==Early life==\nCam was born on November 19, 1984, in [[Huntington Beach, California]],<ref name=\"rocha\">{{cite news|last1=Rocha|first1=Michael James|title=Country singer Cam on her musical journey \u2014 from Oceanside to Nashville to the Grammys|url=http://www.sandiegouniontribune.com/entertainment/music/sd-et-music-cam-20171127-story.html|access-date=29 November 2017|newspaper=The San Diego Union-Tribune|date=November 28, 2017}}</ref> and was raised in [[Lafayette, California]], a suburb in the [[San Francisco Bay Area]].<ref name=SAENash>{{cite news|last1=Malone|first1=Dana|title=Pathway to a record deal: Hard work, circumstance and originality take Cam Ochs 'Down The Road'|url=http://sportsandentertainmentnashville.com/pathway-to-a-record-deal-hard-work-circumstance-and-originality-take-camaron-ochs-down-the-road/|access-date=22 April 2015|publisher=Sports and Entertainment Nashville|date=5 September 2014}}</ref> She also spent time in [[Oceanside, California]], where her grandparents operated a [[ranch]]. They helped develop Cam's appreciation for country music, listening to and performing it regularly.<ref name=BilboarWlecomccount>{{cite magazine|last1=Dauphin|first1=Chuck|title=Welcome To Cam Country: Arista Nashville Singer Has a Short Name, Potentially Long Career|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/the-615/6531920/welcome-to-cam-country-arista-nashville-singer-has-a-short-name|access-date=22 April 2015|magazine=Billboard|date=16 April 2015}}</ref> Pursuing music throughout high school and college, she sang in various choral groups.<ref name=OCOmayinspire>{{cite news|last1=Schadewald|first1=Amber|title=Oakland's Camaron Ochs may inspire folk-pop Barbie|url=http://www.sfbg.com/noise/2010/03/16/oaklands-camaron-ochs-may-inspire-folk-pop-barbie|access-date=22 April 2015|publisher=San Francisco Bay Guardian|date=16 March 2010}}</ref> This included performing in the Contra Costa Children's Chorus, where she learned to sing in 14 languages. She attended the [[University of California, Davis]] as an [[undergraduate education|undergraduate student]], studying psychology.<ref name=\"Smoldering Ballad\">{{cite magazine|last1=Roland|first1=Tom|title=Country Singer Cam Dreams Up a Smoldering Ballad With 'Burning House'|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/6633599/country-singer-cam-dreams-up-a-smoldering-ballad-with-burning-house|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> There, she formed an all-female collegiate [[a cappella]] group called [[The Spokes]] and learned to play the [[guitar]] while studying abroad in the [[Netherlands]]. She developed confidence in playing the instrument on a trip to [[Nepal]]. Taking residency in a rural mountain community, she lived for several weeks with limited electricity and basic needs; in addition, she developed a friendship with various Canadian musicians and started playing the guitar more consistently. In a 2010 interview, Cam stated that she grew more confident in playing once from the trip.<ref name=OCOmayinspire/>\n\nFollowing college, she sporadically performed music but mostly pursued other interests. This included work in research labs, including one at [[Stanford University]]. Yet she remained conflicted about the choices she made.<ref name=\"USA Today\">{{cite news|last1=Ryan|first1=Patrick|title=On the Verge: Cam|url=https://www.usatoday.com/story/life/music/ontheverge/2015/11/01/on-the-verge-cam-burning-house/74596536/|newspaper=[[USA Today]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> A meeting with a college professor influenced Cam's choice to embark on a full-fledged music career. The professor said to her, \"Just picture yourself at 80 years old. Looking back at your life, what would you regret not doing: music or psychology?'\"<ref name=\"USA Today\"/><ref name=\"Billboard Interview\">{{cite magazine|last1=Hight|first1=Jewly|title=Why 'Burning House' Singer Cam Gave Up Psychology for Country Music|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/magazine-feature/6708058/cam-burning-house-women-country-music-psychology|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref>\n\n==Career==\n===2010\u20132014: Early beginnings===\nIn 2010, Cam released her debut studio album titled ''Heartforward'' via the independent Rubber Room label. Credited to her full name of Camaron Ochs, the album contained contemporary [[pop music|pop]] songs.<ref name=\"Allmusic Bio\">{{cite web|last1=Deming|first1=Mark|title=Cam: Biography and History|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/cam-mn0003380333/biography|website=[[Allmusic]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> Amber Schadewald of the ''[[San Francisco Bay Guardian]]'' called the album a brand of [[Folk rock|folk pop]] that \"is light and sweet, with genuine lyrics that ask listeners to live with their 'heartforward'\". Songs written for the project were based on experiences from her trip to Nepal. She promoted ''Heartforward'' through performances in [[Oakland, California|Oakland]] and [[San Francisco, California]], including shows at the Stork Club and Mama Buzz.<ref name=OCOmayinspire/>\n\nCam soon moved to [[Los Angeles, California]], and began collaborating with songwriter and producer [[Tyler Johnson (music)|Tyler Johnson]]. She recorded some demos with Johnson in an attempt to attract [[Faith Hill]], eventually leading to the recordings being heard by [[Tim McGraw]]'s manager.<ref name=SAENash/> Her song \"Fall Madly in Love with You\" was chosen as a track for ''[[Cut to Impress]]'', the 2013 debut album from [[Maggie Rose]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Yes they Cam|url=http://hitsdailydouble.com/news&id=295480|website=HitsDailyDouble|publisher=Hits Digital Ventures|access-date=October 7, 2015|date=April 10, 2015}}</ref><ref name=GlamourMag>{{cite news|last1=Radloff|first1=Jessica|title=Here's What Really Happened Behind the Scenes at the ACM Awards Last Night|url=http://www.glamour.com/entertainment/blogs/obsessed/2015/04/acm-awards-video-photos-red-carpet|access-date=22 April 2015|publisher=Glamour Magazine|date=20 April 2015}}</ref> [[Miley Cyrus]] also recorded one of Cam's songs, \"Maybe You're Right\", on her 2013 album ''[[Bangerz]]''.<ref name=SwedishHDse>{{cite news|last1=Lindqvist|first1=Stefan|title=Camaron Ochs sjunger med Helsingborgsband|url=http://www.hd.se/noje/2013/11/30/camaron-ochs-sjunger-med-helsingborgsband/|access-date=22 April 2015|publisher=HD.se|date=30 November 2013|language=sv}}</ref> The success of these songs led her to  move to [[Nashville, Tennessee]]; there, began writing music for other artists, turning down a publishing deal in attempt to prove herself on her own.<ref name=SAENash/><ref>{{cite news|title=Cameron Ochs keeps it country with rootsy, organic debut|url=http://forthecountryrecord.com/2014/02/12/cameron-ochs-keeps-it-country-with-rootsy-organic-debut-review/|access-date=22 April 2015|publisher=For The Country Record|date=12 February 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150413063846/http://forthecountryrecord.com/2014/02/12/cameron-ochs-keeps-it-country-with-rootsy-organic-debut-review/|archive-date=13 April 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref> She launched a [[Kickstarter]] campaign in 2013 to produce 10 songs with Johnson.<ref name=StamTodayLocals>{{cite news|last1=Inglis|first1=Nicole|title=Country star on the rise with support from Steamboat locals|url=http://www.steamboattoday.com/news/2012/dec/19/country-star-rise-support-steamboat-locals/|access-date=22 April 2015|publisher=Steamboat Today|date=20 December 2012}}</ref> The campaign was supported by producer [[Jeff Bhasker]], known best for his work with artists that include [[Beyonc\u00e9]], [[Fun (band)|fun.]], [[Bruno Mars]], and [[Pink (singer)|P!nk]].<ref name=SAENash/> The same year Cam toured Denmark and Sweden with [[Helsingborg]] band Karavan, having previously collaborated with Anders Mouridsen of the group while in Los Angeles.<ref name=SwedishHDse/>\n\nCam released a [[single (music)|single]] in 2013 titled \"Down This Road\" with the encouragement of manager Lindsay Marias. Through a photo posted on [[Instagram]], local radio director Michael Bryan discovered the song and played it on the air. According to Cam, radio airplay of the single helped her choose which label she wanted to sign to. Ultimately, she chose to meet with [[Doug Morris]], the director of [[Sony Music Entertainment]]. She flew to the label's headquarters in [[New York City]] to meet with him.<ref name=SwedishHDse/> Using only an [[acoustic guitar]], she sang a song she had already been developing, \"[[Burning House]]\". Morris started humming along to the chorus and stated, \"This is the reason why I got into the music business.\" He would later ask her to perform the song at the [[Songwriters Hall of Fame]] ceremony.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Rau|first1=Nate|title=Sony Music CEO Doug Morris touts Nashville up-and-comers|url=http://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/2015/07/24/sony-music-ceo-doug-morris-touts-nashville-up-and-comers/30641039/|website=[[The Tennessean]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> She was soon signed to Sony's country division, [[Arista Nashville]] in 2014<ref name=BilboarTomorrowhits>{{cite magazine|title=Tomorrow's Hits: The Avener's 'Fade Out Lines,' Cam and Young Rising Sons|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/6472726/tomorrow-hits-avener-cam-young-rising-sons|access-date=22 April 2015|magazine=Billboard|date=13 February 2015}}</ref> and toured nationally with [[Dan + Shay]] that same year on their ''Where It All Began'' tour.<ref name=BilboarTomorrowhits/>\n\n===2015\u20132017: Breakthrough===\nIn early 2015, [[Arista Nashville]] released Cam's first single for them, \"[[My Mistake (Cam song)|My Mistake]]\".<ref name=BilboarTomorrowhits/> In March, the song debuted at No. 58 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Country Airplay]] chart.<ref name=BillboardBlackberry>{{cite magazine|last1=Jessen|first1=Wade|title=Blackberry Smoke's 'Roses' Blooms at No. 1 on Top Country Albums|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/6479936/blackberry-smoke-top-country-albums|access-date=22 April 2015|magazine=Billboard|date=19 February 2015}}</ref> The song peaked at number 52 only a few weeks later.<ref>{{cite web|title=New Country Adds|url=http://www.country103.ca/new-music-added/|website=Country 103|access-date=28 December 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160106231408/http://www.country103.ca/new-music-added/|archive-date=2016-01-06|url-status=dead}}</ref> Still using her full name (Camaron Ochs) during the single's promotion, she ultimately shortened it to \"Cam\" because some people found her last name \"too hard to pronounce\".<ref name=BilboarWlecomccount/> \"My Mistake\" preceded Cam's debut [[extended play|EP]], ''[[Welcome to Cam Country]]'', released in March 2015. It contained four songs, with Bhasker and Johnson serving as producers.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Allers|first1=Hannahlee|title=Cam Releases Debut EP|url=http://theboot.com/cam-welcome-to-cam-country-ep/|website=The Boot|date=12 April 2015 |access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.sonymusicnashville.com/press/cam/97966/arista-nashville-recording-artist-cam-reveals-debut-ep-exclusively-spotify|title=Arista Nashville Recording Artist Cam Reveals Debut EP, Exclusively on Spotify|work=Sony Music Nashville|access-date=25 June 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150626130318/http://www.sonymusicnashville.com/press/cam/97966/arista-nashville-recording-artist-cam-reveals-debut-ep-exclusively-spotify|archive-date=26 June 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref> It peaked at No.  31 on the ''Billboard'' [[Top Country Albums]] chart, No. 88 on the [[Billboard 200]], and No. 5 on the [[Top Heatseekers]] survey.<ref>{{cite web|title=''Welcome to Cam Country'' - Cam: Awards|url=http://www.allmusic.com/album/welcome-to-cam-country-mw0002836605/awards|website=[[Allmusic]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref>\n\n\"Burning House\" served as her next single. She performed the song live on the radio program ''[[The Bobby Bones Show]]'', which attracted and fueled attention to the song.<ref name=\"burning\"/> [[Sony Music Entertainment]], of which Arista Nashville is a division, then arranged a meeting and decided to release the track as a single on June 16, 2015, after the song had initial success on the [[iTunes]] charts.<ref name=\"Smoldering Ballad\"/> \"Burning House\" became a top-five hit on the ''Billboard'' [[Hot Country Songs|country songs]] and country airplay charts.<ref name=\"Top Five\">{{cite magazine|last1=Asker|first1=Jim|title=Cam & Emily Ann Roberts' Versions of 'Burning House' Are Both in the Hot Country Songs Top Five|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/6820766/cam-emily-ann-roberts-burning-house-charts|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> It also was the highest-selling female country song of 2015, selling more than 500,000 copies in the United States.<ref>{{cite magazine|last1=Leahey|first1=Andrew|title=Watch Cam Cap Off Smoldering Year With Live 'Burning House'|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/news/watch-cam-cap-off-smoldering-year-with-live-burning-house-20151216|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> In addition the song received nominations at the 2016 [[Grammy Awards]], [[Academy of Country Music Awards]], and [[Country Music Association Awards]].<ref name=\"Best Country Albums\">{{cite magazine|title=Cam, \"Burning House\" - 25 Best Country Songs of 2015|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/25-best-country-songs-of-2015-20151214/cam-burning-house-20151214|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> In January 2022 \"Burning House\" was certified triple-platinum by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]] (RIAA). The success of the song led to the release of her first Arista Nashville album ''[[Untamed (Cam album)|Untamed]]'' on December 11, 2015. Also produced largely by Bhasker and Johnson, it consisted of 11 tracks all co-written by Cam, including all of the songs from the EP.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Reuter|first1=Annie|title=Cam Announces Title, Release Date for Major Label Debut Read More: Cam Announces Title, Release Date for Major Label Debut|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/cam-debut-album-untamed/|website=[[Taste of Country]]|date=2 November 2015 |access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref> It debuted at number two on the Top Country Albums chart and was the highest-selling debut country studio album of 2015.<ref name=\"Top Five\"/> ''Rolling Stone'' ranked the album at number 15 on their list of the \"40 Best Country Albums of 2015\". The magazine commented, \"For an artist at the start of career, Cam already sounds like one of the most secure in the game.\"<ref name=\"Best Country Albums\"/> \"[[Mayday (Cam song)|Mayday]]\" was released as the album's third single in February 2016.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Carr|first1=Courtney|title=Cam Selects 'Mayday' as New Single [LISTEN]|url=http://theboot.com/cam-mayday-song-single/|website=The Boot|date=27 January 2016 |access-date=20 February 2016}}</ref> It was a minor Top 40 hit on the country charts, peaking at number 36 on ''Billboard'' Country Airplay. \n\nIn October 2017, Cam announced a new single titled [[Diane (Cam song)|\"Diane\"]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/country/news/hear-cams-jolene-inspired-new-song-diane-w510372|title=Hear Cam's Supercharged, 'Jolene'-Inspired New Song 'Diane'|last=Betts|first=Stephen L.|date=October 27, 2017|work=Rolling Stone Country|access-date=27 October 2017}}</ref> She promoted the song with several live performances including on [[Good Morning America]],<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.countryliving.com/life/entertainment/a19681578/cam-diane-song/|title=Watch Dolly Parton Surprise Country Singer Cam On 'Good Morning America'|last=Matthews|first=Lauren|date=4 April 2018|work=Country Living|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> ''[[The Late Late Show with James Corden]]'',<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/8343549/late-late-show-cam-diane|title=Cam Gives Mesmerizing Performance of 'Diane' on 'The Late Late Show'|last=Cummings-Grady|first=Mackenzie|date=17 April 2018|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> and as a duet with a contestant on [[American Idol (season 16)|season 16 of ''American Idol'']].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://theboot.com/cam-american-idol-effie-passero-diane-shannon-ohara-burning-house/|title=Cam Duets with 'American Idol' Contestants on 'Diane,' 'Burning House'|last=Stefano|first=Angela|date=17 April 2018|work=The Boot|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> In April 2018, \"Diane\" was added to the [[BBC Radio 2]] A-list and hit No. 1 on iTunes for 5 weeks. Also in 2017, Cam, along with [[Sam Smith (singer)|Sam Smith]] and Tyler Johnson, co-wrote the song \"Palace\" for Smith's 2017 album ''[[The Thrill of It All (Sam Smith album)|The Thrill of It All]]'' and providing background vocals and guitar to the track.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://people.com/country/cam-wrote-sam-smith-song-we-had-same-heartache/|title=Country Star Cam on Writing a Song for Sam Smith's New Album: We Had the 'Same Heartache'|last=Nelson|first=Jeff|date=3 November 2017|work=People|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> The song saw international success and was highlighted in the Holiday \"Sway\" commercial for [[Apple Inc.|Apple]] which led to its reaching No. 1 on the Billboard Top TV Commercials Chart.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/8093860/sam-smith-palace-apple-ad-top-tv-commercials-chart-number-one|title=Sam Smith's 'Palace' Hits No. 1 on Top TV Commercials Chart for December|last=Zellner|first=Xander|date=11 January 2018|magazine=Billboard|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> The widespread embrace of \"Palace\" included much international success, specifically in [[Japan]], where Smith performed the song on multiple TV talk shows. Cam opened for Smith on the Summer US leg of his 2018 The Thrill Of It All Tour.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/cam-joins-sam-smiths-thrill-of-it-all-tour-629146/|title=Cam Joins Sam Smith's Thrill of It All Tour|last=Betts|first=Stephen L.|date=7 June 2018|magazine=Rolling Stone|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> Cam has also shared the stage with [[Tim McGraw]] and [[Faith Hill]] on their [[Soul2Soul: The World Tour|Soul2Soul Tour]]<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/tim-mcgraw-faith-hills-soul2soul-tour-taps-devin-dawson-caitlyn-smith-127866/|title=Tim McGraw, Faith Hill's Soul2Soul Tour Taps Devin Dawson, Caitlyn Smith|last=Parton|first=Chris|date=19 March 2018|magazine=Rolling Stone|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> as well as [[Harry Styles]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://people.com/country/harry-styles-invited-cam-open-nashville-concert-better-than-hype/|title=Harry Styles Invited Country Star Cam to Open His Nashville Show: 'He's Even Better Than All the Hype'|last=Nelson|first=Jeff|date=29 September 2017|work=People|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref>\n\n===2018\u2013present: Transition to RCA ===\nIn July 2018, Cam released \"Road to Happiness\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/cam-road-to-happiness/|title=Cam Ponders the Real Meaning of Joy in 'Road to Happiness'|last=Whitaker|first=Sterling|date=13 July 2018|work=Taste of Country|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> and parted ways with Arista Nashville.<ref name=\"triple tigers signing\">{{cite magazine |title=Cam Signs with Nashville's Triple Tiers Label in Partnership with RCA New York |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/9410902/cam-signs-nashville-triple-tigers-partnership-rca-new-york |access-date=June 29, 2020 |magazine=Billboard}}</ref> In 2019, she provided vocals for [[Diplo]]'s song \"[[So Long (Diplo song)|So Long]]\" for his ''[[Diplo Presents Thomas Wesley, Chapter 1: Snake Oil]]'' album.<ref name=\":0\">{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/diplo-cam-so-long-thomas-wesley-828677/|title=Song You Need to Know: Diplo and Cam, 'So Long'|last=Freeman|first=Jon|date=2019-05-02|magazine=Rolling Stone|language=en-US|access-date=2020-02-13}}</ref>\n\nOn June 29, 2020, it was announced that Cam had signed a new partnership for radio promotion with Nashville-based [[Triple Tigers]] in a joint venture with her label [[RCA Records]]. \"Classic\" was released on July 17, 2020, as her first country radio single since \"Diane\" in 2017. Her critically acclaimed sophomore album, ''[[The Otherside (album)|The Otherside]]'', was released on October 30, 2020.<ref>{{Cite web |title=The Otherside by Cam |url=https://music.apple.com/nz/album/the-otherside/1523527625}}</ref> For this release, she once again enlisted producers [[Tyler Johnson (musician)|Tyler Johnson]] ([[Harry Styles]], [[Miley Cyrus]]) and [[Jeff Bhasker]] ([[Kanye West]], [[Alicia Keys]]). The record featured the international Jolene-in-reverse hit \u201c[[Diane (Cam song)|Diane]],\u201d the song \u201cTill There's Nothing Left,\u201d plus songwriting from [[Avicii]], [[Harry Styles]], [[Jack Antonoff]], and [[Sam Smith]]. <ref name=\"triple tigers signing\"/><ref name=\"Rolling Stone\">{{Cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/cam-till-theres-nothing-left-952115/|title=Cam Addresses Sex and Swagger on New Song, 'Till There's Nothing Left'|last=Freeman|first=Jon|date=2020-02-13|magazine=Rolling Stone|language=en-US|access-date=2020-02-13}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Cam preps \"magical\" new song, \"Redwood Tree\" |url=http://www.hotcountry931.com/2020/05/cam-preps-magical-new-song-redwood-tree/ |website=Hot Country 931 |access-date=28 May 2020}}</ref>\n\nIn 2024, she contributed songwriting, production and backing vocals for [[Beyonc\u00e9]]'s ''[[Cowboy Carter]]'' album (\u201cAmerican Requiem,\u201d \u201cAmen,\u201d \u201cProtector,\u201d \u201cTyrant,\u201d \u201cDaughter\u201d).<ref>{{cite web | url=https://variety.com/2024/music/news/cam-beyonce-cowboy-carter-writing-production-1235963667/ | title=Singer-Songwriter Cam Discusses Working on Five Tracks for Beyonc\u00e9's Cowboy Carter: She's Just Such a Creative Genius | date=8 April 2024 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Cam Post on Twitter |url=https://twitter.com/camcountry/status/1773788015346974744 |website=twitter.com |publisher=X Corp. |access-date=2024-04-07}}</ref>\n\n==Artistry==\nCam was exposed to classic country music at an early age from the time spent on her grandparents' ranch. They introduced her to the musical sounds of [[Patsy Cline]], [[Bonnie Raitt]] and [[Willie Nelson]].<ref name=BilboarWlecomccount/> She was largely influenced by the vocal phrasing of Cline and [[Ray Charles]]. She also developed an appreciation for [[the Chicks]] and the [[Indigo Girls]], commenting that she was \"so into those female harmonies\". She additionally cites [[Bob Dylan]], [[Joni Mitchell]], and [[Randy Newman]] as influences on her songwriting style.<ref name=\"Billboard Interview\"/> Although she has a variety of musical influences, Cam stated that country music is where she felt most connected to. In a 2015 interview with ''[[Rolling Stone]]'', she explained her reasoning: \"I grew up singing in a lot of different languages and a lot of world music choirs, so I have a lot of musical influences. But the songwriting structure of country music is the standard in my mind. ... That structure seems to feel the most homey to me.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|title=Cam - 10 New Country Artists You Need to Know: Spring 2015|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/10-new-country-artists-you-need-to-know-spring-2015-20150505/cam-20150505|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=28 December 2015}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nIn September 2015, Cam became engaged to Adam Weaver, a business broker with First Choice Business Brokers in Nashville.<ref>{{cite web|last1=McClellan|first1=Laura|title=Cam Shows Off New Bling|url=http://tasteofcountry.com/cam-engaged/|website=Taste of Country|date=9 September 2015 |access-date=22 July 2016}}</ref> In October 2016, the couple married in a small ceremony in a California desert.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Anderson|first1=Danielle|title=See Cam's Stunning Wedding Album!|url=http://people.com/country/cam-wedding-album-marries-adam-weaver/|website=People|access-date=11 October 2016}}</ref> In December 2019, she gave birth to her first child, Lucy. Shortly after giving birth, Cam posted on social media that she was a \"breech at 39wks, a next-day c-section (ouch) & here we are... three of us now.\"<ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Iasimone |first1=Ashley |title=Cam Gives Birth to Baby Lucy Marvel: See the Photos |url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/8546960/cam-baby-birth-announcement |magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] |access-date=24 February 2020}}</ref>\n\nCam is a vocal advocate for music education and inclusion. She spoke on the psychology of music in her 2017 [[TEDx talk|TEDx Talk]] at the University of Nevada.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/5-things-we-learned-from-cams-tedx-talk-193313/|title=5 Things We Learned From Cam's TEDx Talk|last=Parton|first=Chris|date=7 March 2017|magazine=Rolling Stone|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> Cam is on the [[Academy of Country Music]] (ACM) Board and was invited to join [[The Recording Academy]]'s Task Force on Diversity and Inclusion in 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/news/recording-academy-names-diversity-and-inclusion-task-force-members/|title= Recording Academy Names Diversity And Inclusion Task Force Members|date=9 May 2018|work=Grammy.com|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref> In 2018, Cam joined the speaker list on [[Hello Sunshine (company)|Hello Sunshine]] x Together Live's touring event<ref>{{cite web|url=http://togetherlive.com/about/|title= Our Stories Travel|access-date=2 January 2019}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n{{main|Cam discography}}\n'''Studio albums'''\n* This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Jaron_Lowenstein","to":"Jaron Lowenstein"}],"pages":{"26137601":{"pageid":26137601,"ns":0,"title":"Jaron Lowenstein","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American singer|bot=PearBOT 5}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Jaron Lowenstein\n| image           =\n| caption         =\n| birth_name      = Jaron David Lowenstein\n| alias           = Jaron and the Long Road to Love\n| birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|1974|03|18}}<ref name=\"Associated Press\">{{cite web | url = http://www.boston.com/news/history/articles/2011/03/18/today_in_history/ | title = Today in History | work = [[The Associated Press]] | date = March 18, 2011 | quote = Evan and Jaron Lowenstein are 37}}</ref>\n| origin          = [[Tucker, Georgia|Tucker]], [[Georgia (U.S. state)|Georgia]], U.S.\n| genre           = [[Country pop]]\n| years_active    = 1994\u2013present\n| label           = Jaronwood<br>[[Universal Republic Records]]<br>[[Big Machine Records|Big Machine]]<br>[[Republic Nashville]]<br>Nine North\n| past_member_of= [[Evan and Jaron]]\n}}\n\n'''Jaron David Lowenstein''' (born March 18, 1974) is an American singer who formerly recorded with his [[identical twin]] brother, Evan, in the musical duo [[Evan and Jaron]]. As '''Jaron and the Long Road to Love''', he released his debut [[single (music)|single]], \"Pray for You\" to country radio in November 2009. This song reached the top 15 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] charts, and is included on the album ''[[Getting Dressed in the Dark]]''. The second single, \"That's Beautiful to Me\", was released in September 2010.\n\n== Life and career ==\nLowenstein was born in [[Tucker, Georgia]], the son of Leslie (n\u00e9e Diamond) and Charles Lowenstein. He was raised in an [[Orthodox Judaism|Orthodox Jewish]] family, and attended [[Greenfield Hebrew Academy]] and [[Yeshiva Atlanta|Yeshiva High School]] (which have since merged to form the [[Atlanta Jewish Academy]])<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.atlantajewish.com/content/2004/evanandjaron.html|title=American Jewish Life Magazine|website=Atlantajewish.com|accessdate=7 June 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100212153007/http://www.atlantajewish.com/content/2004/evanandjaron.html|archive-date=12 February 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.ajc.com/radio-tv-talk/2010/08/30/former-atlanta-rocker-jaron-of-evan-and-jaron-lassos-a-hit-in-country-music/ |title=Former Atlanta rocker Jaron of Evan and Jaron lassos a hit in country music &#124; Radio & TV Talk |accessdate=July 18, 2012 |url-status=dead |archiveurl=https://web.archive.org/web/20120514114718/http://blogs.ajc.com/radio-tv-talk/2010/08/30/former-atlanta-rocker-jaron-of-evan-and-jaron-lassos-a-hit-in-country-music/ |archivedate=May 14, 2012 }}</ref> Through his mother, he is related (by marriage) to actor [[Logan Lerman]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.imdb.com/name/nm0503567/bio|title=Logan Lerman|website=IMDb.com|accessdate=7 June 2016}}</ref> In the late 1990s and early 2000s, Lowenstein recorded with his [[identical twin]] brother, Evan, in the [[pop music|pop]] duo [[Evan and Jaron]].<ref name=\"boot\">{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2010/03/12/jaron-long-road-love-songs/|title=Jaron Prescribes Music as Antidote to Tough Times|date=March 12, 2010|work=The Boot|accessdate=March 12, 2010}}</ref> Evan and Jaron charted three [[single (music)|singles]], including \"[[Crazy for This Girl]],\" which reached number 15 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] charts in 2000.<ref name=\"weekly\">{{cite journal|date=1 February 2010|title=Who's New|journal=[[Country Weekly]]|volume=17|issue=5|pages=17|issn=1074-3235}}</ref> The duo split up in 2003 so that Evan could focus on raising his family.<ref name=\"boot\"/>\n\nJaron co-wrote and recorded his first solo single, \"[[Pray for You (Jaron and the Long Road to Love song)|Pray for You]]\", as Jaron and the Long Road to Love in late 2009.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://blog.cmt.com/2009-11-20/jaron-lowenstein-offers-a-prayer-for-your-ex/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20091123193835/http://blog.cmt.com/2009-11-20/jaron-lowenstein-offers-a-prayer-for-your-ex/|url-status=dead|archive-date=November 23, 2009|title=Jaron Lowenstein Offers a Prayer for Your Ex|last=Bonaguro|first=Alison|date=November 20, 2009|work=[[Country Music Television|CMT]]|accessdate=November 24, 2009}}</ref> Starting in February 2010, [[Big Machine Records]] assumed promotion of the single and a forthcoming album, which was distributed through a partnership of Jaron's Jaronwood label and [[Universal Republic]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.allaccess.com/net-news/archive/story/71765/jaron-long-run-ink-deal-with-universal-republic?ref=search|title=Jaron & Long Run Ink Deal With Universal Republic|date=March 5, 2010|work=All Access|accessdate=March 25, 2010}}</ref> The song reached the top 40 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Country Songs]] chart and the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]].\n\nJaron told [[Technorati]] that the song \"wasn't started or pushed by some major label or organization. I would love to take the credit for its success, but honestly this is something fans want and they are the ones calling radio to have them play it.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://technorati.com/entertainment/article/even-celebrities-arent-immune-to-valentines1/|title=Even Celebrities Aren't Immune To Valentine's Day Pressure|date=February 16, 2010|work=Technorati|accessdate=March 26, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100219010143/http://technorati.com/entertainment/article/even-celebrities-arent-immune-to-valentines1/|archive-date=February 19, 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref> Hank Friedmann directed a [[music video]] for the song, which has aired on [[CMT Pure Country]] (CMT Pure) and [[Great American Country]] (GAC).<ref name=\"cmtvid\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/videos/jaron-and-the-long-road-to-love/467605/pray-for-you.jhtml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100108012801/http://www.cmt.com/videos/jaron-and-the-long-road-to-love/467605/pray-for-you.jhtml|url-status=dead|archive-date=January 8, 2010|title=Music video for \"Pray for You\"|work=CMT|accessdate=March 23, 2010}}</ref> A second video, which includes [[Jaime Pressly]], debuted in April 2010.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://blog.cmt.com/2010-04-12/jaron-gives-the-back-story-in-new-pray-for-you/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110725192819/http://blog.cmt.com/2010-04-12/jaron-gives-the-back-story-in-new-pray-for-you/|url-status=dead|archive-date=July 25, 2011|title=Jaron Gives the Back Story in New \"Pray for You\"|last=Bonaguro|first=Alison|date=April 12, 2010|work=CMT|accessdate=April 12, 2010}}</ref>\n\nHis debut album, ''Getting Dressed in the Dark'', was released on June 22, 2010.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.theboot.com/2010/04/07/jaron-long-road-to-love-getting-dressed-in-the-dark-new-album/|title=Jaron Gets 'Dressed' for New Album|last=Hughes|first=Donna|date=April 7, 2010|work=The Boot|accessdate=April 12, 2010}}</ref> The album's second single is \"That's Beautiful to Me\", which debuted on the country chart at number 59 in September 2010.\n\nIn early 2011, Lowenstein parted ways with [[Big Machine Records]] and [[Republic Nashville]]. Despite leaving the label, a third single from ''Getting Dressed in the Dark'', \"It's a Good Thing\", was released on April 18, 2011, with promotion from Nine North Records. However, the single failed to chart.\n\nOn May 31, 2011, Lowenstein released \"Beautiful Lies\", which features [[Big Kenny]], one-half of the [[country music]] duo [[Big & Rich]]. The song is the lead-off single to Lowenstein's second album. The song also failed to chart.\n\nIn 2011, eleven songs were released as a self-titled album by the band Cordovas. The band is made out of [[Joe Firstman]], Jaron Lowenstein, Jon Loyd, Johnny Gray, Parker Gins and Toby Weaver.  The album was made available as a free download on the band's official website <ref name=\"Official Site\">{{cite web|url=http://www.cordovasband.com|title=Cordovas|date=2011}}</ref> as well as other traditional paying outlets.\n\nThe songs \"Old Dog\" and \"All I Found\" had videos released online.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Catherine_McGrath","to":"Catherine McGrath"}],"pages":{"57116475":{"pageid":57116475,"ns":0,"title":"Catherine McGrath","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|Northern Irish singer and songwriter}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=April 2022}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name         = Catherine McGrath\n| image        =Catherine McGrath (52338298859).jpg\n| caption      =McGrath in 2022\n| birth_name   = Catherine McGrath\n| alias        =\n| birth_date   = {{birth date and age|1997|6|9|df=y}}\n| birth_place  = [[Rostrevor]], [[County Down]], Northern Ireland\n| origin       =\n| genre        = [[Country pop]]\n| occupation   = {{hlist|Singer|songwriter}}\n| instrument   = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar}}\n| years_active = 2016\u2013present\n| label        = [[Warner Bros. Records]]\n| website      = {{URL|www.imcatherinemcgrath.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Catherine McGrath''' (born 9 June 1997)<ref>{{cite web|title=Catherine McGrath Biography|url=http://www.countrymusicbookingagency.com/musician/catherine-mcgrath.php|website=Country Music Booking Agency|accessdate=13 April 2018|archive-date=13 April 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180413190431/http://www.countrymusicbookingagency.com/musician/catherine-mcgrath.php|url-status=live}}</ref> is a Northern Irish [[country music]] singer and songwriter.\n\n==Career==\n===Early life===\nBorn in [[Rostrevor]], Northern Ireland, McGrath learned guitar from her grandmother, who taught her to play and sing \"[[The Lion Sleeps Tonight]]\".{{cn|date=July 2023}} McGrath's parents are both musicians and were frequent performers at the annual Fiddler's Green Music Festival held in [[County Down]], Northern Ireland. McGrath honed her skills by observing her parents on-stage and by watching instructional videos online. McGrath took up songwriting, and in addition to performing her own material, she began making homemade videos of herself performing current pop hits, which she then posted online. McGrath has said that her country music influences include [[Taylor Swift]], [[Kacey Musgraves]], [[Kelsea Ballerini]], [[Brad Paisley]], and [[Rascal Flatts]];<ref>{{cite web|title=Catherine McGrath|url=http://wilfulpublicity.co.uk/artists/catherine-mcgrath|website=Wilful Publicity|publisher=Wilful Publicity|accessdate=13 April 2018|archive-date=14 April 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180414010539/http://wilfulpublicity.co.uk/artists/catherine-mcgrath|url-status=live}}</ref> she credits Swift's song \"[[Love Story (Taylor Swift song)|Love Story]]\" in particular for introducing her to country music at the age of 12.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Sargeant|first1=Glenn|title=CATHERINE MCGRATH \u2013 ONE BRIGHT STAR|url=http://justlistentothis.co.uk/interviews/catherine-mcgrath-one-bright-star/|website=Just Listen To This|publisher=Just Listen To This|accessdate=13 April 2018|archive-date=13 April 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180413191525/http://justlistentothis.co.uk/interviews/catherine-mcgrath-one-bright-star/|url-status=live}}</ref>\n\n===2016\u2013present: Signing with Warner Bros. Records and debut studio album===\nMcGrath's videos attracted the attention of Instrumental, a company that finds talent online and grooms them for larger success. She moved to [[London]] to work for the company, and after only a few months, began travelling to [[Nashville, Tennessee|Nashville]] for songwriting and studio sessions.<ref>{{cite web|last1=Deming|first1=Mark|title=Catherine McGrath, Biography & History|url=https://www.allmusic.com/artist/catherine-mcgrath-mn0003569043/biography|website=AllMusic|publisher=AllMusic|accessdate=13 April 2018|archive-date=13 April 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180413190015/https://www.allmusic.com/artist/catherine-mcgrath-mn0003569043/biography|url-status=live}}</ref> In the summer of 2016, McGrath signed with Warner Bros. She recorded and released her first solo [[Extended play|EP]] ''One'' in December later that same year. Her major label debut album, ''Talk of This Town'', was released on 27 July 2018.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://rocknloadmag.com/album-review/catherine-mcgrath-talk-of-this-town-album-review/|title=Catherine McGrath \u2013 \u2018Talk Of This Town\u2019 \u2013 Album Review|date=2018-07-24|website=R   o   c   k    'N'    L   o   a  d|language=en-GB|access-date=2019-08-01|archive-date=1 August 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190801193742/https://rocknloadmag.com/album-review/catherine-mcgrath-talk-of-this-town-album-review/|url-status=live}}</ref> McGrath played a set at the [[C2C: Country to Country]] festival in 2019 and joined [[Hunter Hayes]] on stage at the [[O2 Arena (London)|O2 Arena]] to duet on their song \"Don't Let Me Forget\".\n\n== Discography ==\n=== Studio albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Album\n|-\n| rowspan=\"2\"|2018\n! scope=\"row\"| \"Paperboy\"\n| rowspan=\"2\"| [[Megan McKenna]]\n| rowspan=\"2\"| ''[[Story of Me]]''\n|-\n! scope=\"row\"| \"[[High Heeled Shoes (song)|High Heeled Shoes]]\"\n|-\n|}\n\n== Recognition ==\nIn 2018, McGrath was fan-voted as the winner of the International Emerging Artist of The Year award in the Music For A New Generation Awards, run by Australian country radio program, [[Planet Country with Big Stu & MJ|Planet Country]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.planetcountryradio.com.au/mfang-awards-2018|title=Planet Country MFANG 2018|date=2018-12-10|website=Planet Country Radio Show|access-date=2018-12-14|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181113212302/https://www.planetcountryradio.com.au/mfang-awards-2018|archive-date=2018-11-13|url-status=dead}}</ref>\n\n==References==\n{{Reflist}}\n\n==External links==\n* {{official website|https://www.imcatherinemcgrath.com}}\n*{{Commons category-inline}}\n\n{{Authority control}}\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Mcgrath, Catherine}}\n[[Category:1997 births]]\n[[Category:Living people]]\n[[Category:21st-century singers from Northern Ireland]]\n[[Category:British women songwriters]]\n[[Category:British country singers]]\n[[Category:Country pop musicians]]"}]}}}}{"batchcomplete":"","warnings":{"main":{"*":"Subscribe to the mediawiki-api-announce mailing list at <https://lists.wikimedia.org/postorius/lists/mediawiki-api-announce.lists.wikimedia.org/> for notice of API deprecations and breaking changes. Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Sons_of_Sylvia","to":"Sons of Sylvia"}],"pages":{"14434697":{"pageid":14434697,"ns":0,"title":"Sons of Sylvia","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country pop trio}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Sons of Sylvia\n| image                 = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| alias = The Clark Brothers\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Virginia]], [[United States]]\n| genre               = [[Country pop]]\n| years_active        = 2007\u20132012\n| label               = [[Show Dog-Universal Music|Universal South]]<br />[[Interscope Records|Interscope]]\n| spinoff_of = [[The Clark Family Experience]]\n| past_members     = Adam Clark<br />Ashley Clark<br />Austin Clark\n}}\n'''Sons of Sylvia''', originally known as '''The Clark Brothers''', was an American [[country pop]] trio composed of three brothers with the surname Clark: Adam ([[guitar]], [[mandolin]]), Ashley ([[lead vocals]], [[fiddle]], mandolin, guitar) and Austin ([[background vocals]], [[resonator guitar]]). All three, along with their three other brothers Aaron, Andrew, and Alan, originally comprised a sextet called [[The Clark Family Experience]]. Sons of Sylvia released its debut album in April 2010.\n\n==History==\nBrothers Adam, Ashley, Austin, Aaron, Andrew, and Alan Clark, natives of [[Rocky Mount, Virginia]], founded a family band in the late 1990s called [[The Clark Family Experience]]. The band recorded one album for [[Curb Records]] in 2000 and charted in the Top 20 on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' country singles charts with \"[[Meanwhile Back at the Ranch]].\" The Clark Family Experience disbanded in 2002 after filing for [[Chapter 7 bankruptcy]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.roanoke.com/entertainment/insideout/podcasts/wb/143359 |title=Clark Brothers still in it; taking one show at a time |access-date=2008-07-09 |last=Dickens |first=Tad |date=2007-12-14 |work=Roanoke Times |archive-url=https://archive.today/20120910221103/http://www.roanoke.com/entertainment/insideout/podcasts/wb/143359 |archive-date=2012-09-10 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\nIn 2007, Adam, Ashley, and Austin began playing as The Clark Brothers. Under this name, the trio won the top prize in the [[Fox Networks]] talent competition ''[[The Next Great American Band]]'', and subsequently signed to 19 Recordings.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.sonsofsylvia.com/bio/default.aspx |title=Biography |publisher=Sons of Sylvia |date= |accessdate=2012-03-29}}</ref> The band renamed itself Sons of Sylvia in October 2009.<ref name=\"weekly\">{{cite journal|date=2009-08-31|title=The Scoop|journal=[[Country Weekly]]|volume=16|issue=38|pages=12\u201313|issn=1074-3235}}</ref>\n\nSons of Sylvia appeared on the song \"What Can I Say\" on [[Carrie Underwood]]'s third album, ''[[Play On (Carrie Underwood album)|Play On]]''. The band had a connection with Underwood through Ashley, who toured with Carrie as her fiddle player from 2005-2009. The band performed \"What Can I Say\" with Carrie Underwood on December 7, 2009, on ''Carrie Underwood: An All Star Holiday Special''. Sons of Sylvia also joined Carrie on her 2010 \"[[Play On Tour]]\".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.carrieunderwoodofficial.com/us/news/%E2%80%9Cplay-tour%E2%80%9D-kicks-thursday |title=\"Play On Tour\" Kicks Off This Thursday! &#124; The Official Carrie Underwood Site |publisher=Carrieunderwoodofficial.com |date=2010-04-09 |accessdate=2012-03-29}}</ref>  The band performed their debut single, \"Love Left to Lose,\" on the April 28, 2010 results show episode of ''[[American Idol]]'' and were introduced by Carrie Underwood.<ref>{{cite AV media|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oJoVv8RBvt0| archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100429040228/http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=oJoVv8RBvt0| archive-date=2010-04-29 | url-status=dead|title=YouTube|website=Youtube.com}}</ref>\n\nThe group are cousins to [[Ryan Tedder]], lead singer for [[OneRepublic]], who co-wrote and produced the group's debut single, \"Love Left to Lose\".<ref>[http://www.theboot.com/2010/08/11/sons-of-sylvia-love-left-to-lose-lyrics/ Sons of Sylvia, 'Love Left to Lose' - Story Behind the Lyrics]. Theboot.com</ref> The album's second single, \"I'll Know You\", was released to radio in late 2010 but did not chart. In February 2012, Sons Of Sylvia were dropped from Interscope Records. Ashley signed with [[I.R.S. Records]] as a solo artist in 2015.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.themusicintro.com/2015/03/first-listen-ashley-clark-greyhound.html |title=The Music Intro: First Listen: Ashley Clark // Greyhound |website=www.themusicintro.com |access-date=17 January 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150324062147/http://www.themusicintro.com/2015/03/first-listen-ashley-clark-greyhound.html |archive-date=24 March 2015 |url-status=dead}}</ref> As fate would have it Ashley Clark got dropped, when I.R.S. Records ceased trading in mid December 2015.\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:10em;\"| Title\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Album details\n! colspan=\"2\"| Peak chart<br />positions\n|- style=\"font-size:smaller;\"\n! style=\"width:40px;\"| [[Billboard 200|US]]<br /><ref>{{cite magazine|url={{BillboardURLbyName|artist=sons of sylvia|chart=all}}|title=Sons of Sylvia Album & Song Chart History - Billboard 200|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|publisher=[[Prometheus Global Media]]|accessdate=October 16, 2010}}</ref>\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Shelly_West","to":"Shelly West"}],"pages":{"5396568":{"pageid":5396568,"ns":0,"title":"Shelly West","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|American country music singer (born 1958)}}\n{{Multiple issues|\n{{BLP sources|date=June 2012}}\n{{one source|date=June 2012}}\n}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name            = Shelly West\n|image           = \n|caption         = \n|image_size      = (220)\n|background      = solo_singer\n|birth_name      = \n|birth_date      = {{Birth date and age|1956|05|23|mf=y}}\n|origin          = [[Cleveland]], [[Ohio]], U.S.\n|instrument      = Vocals\n|genre           = [[Country pop]]\n|occupation      = Singer\n|years_active    = 1981&ndash;1992<br>2012&ndash;present\n|label           = {{flatlist|\n*[[K-tel]]\n*[[Warner Bros. Records|Warner Bros.]]\n*[[Viva Records (U.S.)|Viva]]\n*[[Var\u00e8se Sarabande]]}}\n|associated_acts = {{flatlist|\n*[[David Frizzell]]\n*[[Dottie West]]}}\n}}\n'''Shelly West''' (born May 23, 1956) is an [[United States|American]] [[country music]] [[singing|singer]]. Her mother was the country music star [[Dottie West]], whose career spanned three decades. The younger West reached her peak in popularity during the 1980s before mostly retiring in the wake of her mother's death.\n\n==Biography==\n\n===1981\u20131987===\nWest was born in [[Cleveland, Ohio]], and rose to prominence at the same time as her mother Dottie was reinventing herself as a [[country pop]] star, and Shelly's style was not significantly different from that of her mother's. West is best known for her hit [[duet]]s with [[David Frizzell]], especially their number-one hit \"[[You're the Reason God Made Oklahoma]]\". She also was a successful solo artist, having her own number-one hit, \"[[Jos\u00e9 Cuervo (song)|Jos\u00e9 Cuervo]]\" in 1983. West was married to [[Gary Hood]] 1983-2000.\n\n===1987\u20131992: Retirement===\nWest did reunite with Frizzell for a few shows in the late 1980s. West married Garry Hood in 1983 and had twin sons.<ref>[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p137248/biography|pure_url=yes}} Biography at Allmusic.com]</ref> In 1990, Shelly toured with her mother, Dottie; together, they were popular on the road. On August 30, 1991, Dottie was involved in a major car accident, eventually dying five days later, on September 4, from injuries sustained in the accident. West was a technical adviser for a television biopic about her mother's life, ''[[Big Dreams and Broken Hearts: The Dottie West Story]]'', produced by and starring actress [[Michele Lee]]. At that point, amid major changes in the country music industry that impacted the careers of many established country stars, the younger West retired to focus on her family.\n\n===Post-retirement===\nIn June 2005, CMT honored Shelly and her duet partner, David Frizzell, when they were voted number six on its ''100 Greatest Duets Special''. Although they did not perform any songs, Shelly West and David Frizzell appeared on the special, for which West was interviewed. West appeared on numerous episodes of ''Country Family Reunion'' on [[RFD-TV]].\n\nWest has returned to performing occasionally since 2012. She reunited with David Frizzell for two shows on October 13, 2012, at the God and Country Theater in [[Branson, Missouri]]. The duo played another show on November 2, 2013 at the Americana Theater in Branson.\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:22em;\"| Title\n! rowspan=\"2\" style=\"width:18em;\"| Album details\n! This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Tenille_Townes","to":"Tenille Townes"}],"pages":{"55797013":{"pageid":55797013,"ns":0,"title":"Tenille Townes","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{short description|Canadian country music singer}}\n{{distinguish|Toni Tennille|Tenille Arts}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Tenille Townes\n| image           = TenilleTownes2023.jpg\n| image_size      =\n| landscape       = <!-- yes, if wide image, otherwise leave blank -->\n| alt             =\n| caption         = Townes performing at The Stoller Hall in [[Manchester]], England, 2023\n| birth_name      = Tenille Nicole Nadkrynechny\n| alias           =\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|1994|01|20}}\n| birth_place     =\n| origin          = [[Grande Prairie]], [[Alberta]], Canada\n| genre           = [[Country pop]]\n| occupation      = {{hlist|Singer|songwriter}}\n| instrument      = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar}}\n| years_active    = 2009\u2013present\n| label           = {{hlist|[[Royalty Records|Royalty]]|[[Sony Music Nashville|Columbia Nashville]]|[[RCA Records|RCA]]}}\n| website         = {{URL|tenilletownes.com}}\n}}\n'''Tenille Nicole Townes''' (born '''Nadkrynechny'''; January 20, 1994) is a Canadian [[country music]] singer from [[Grande Prairie]], [[Alberta]]. In 2011, at the age of 17, she was nominated for a [[Canadian Country Music Association|Canadian Country Music Award]] for Female Artist of the Year.<ref>{{cite news|last=MacLeod|first=Reinisa|date=August 2011|title=Tenille takes on the country|url=http://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/ArticleDisplay.aspx?e=3273711|newspaper=[[Media in Grande Prairie|Daily Herald-Tribune]]|accessdate=12 September 2011|archive-date=22 March 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120322131535/http://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/ArticleDisplay.aspx?e=3273711|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|last=Griwkowsky|first=Fish|date=27 July 2011|title=Two Edmonton country stars nominated for music awards|url=http://www.canada.com/story_print.html?id=5169029&sponsor=|newspaper=[[Edmonton Journal]]|accessdate=20 September 2011}}{{Dead link|date=June 2018 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=no }}</ref>\n\n== Biography ==\nTownes was raised in Grande Prairie, Alberta, and attended Peace Wapiti Academy high school.<ref name=national>{{cite news|last=Wood|first=Damien|date=2010|title=Tenille's song hits national radio|url=http://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/ArticleDisplay.aspx?archive=true&e=2157444|newspaper=Daily Herald-Tribune|accessdate=20 September 2011|archive-date=22 March 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120322131624/http://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/ArticleDisplay.aspx?archive=true&e=2157444|url-status=dead}}</ref> She was introduced to country music by her parents and grandparents during trips in the family car.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Wickstrom |first1=Matt |title=Interview: Tenille Townes Reveals Her True Self on Stellar New EP 'Masquerades' |website=The Boot |url=https://theboot.com/tenille-townes-masquerades-interview/ |access-date=19 September 2022 |date=2022-05-11}}</ref> At the age of nine, she attended a concert by Shania Twain during her [[Up! Tour]] bearing a sign asking for chance to sing with Twain on stage, which Twain granted.<ref name=npr>{{cite web |last1=Hight |first1=Jewly |title=Nashville's Newest Voice |website=[[NPR]] |url=https://www.npr.org/sections/therecord/2018/05/07/608976983/nashvilles-newest-voice |access-date=20 September 2022}}</ref> In 2009, she released the single \"Home Now\", a song she wrote from the perspective of a daughter whose father is posted in the [[War in Afghanistan (2001\u2013present)|war in Afghanistan]], a topic she learned about in school.<ref name=national /><ref name=Sperounes>{{cite news|last=Sperounes|first=Sandra|date=11 November 2009|title=Alberta teen pays tribute to war heroes: Home Now captures national sentiment|newspaper=[[Edmonton Journal]]|page=D1}}</ref> The track was produced by country musician [[Duane Steele]].<ref name=Sperounes />\n\nTownes released her first album, ''Real'', in June 2011.<ref>{{cite news|last=Ilika|first=Dan|date=June 2011|title=Dream becomes 'Real' for Tenille|url=http://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/ArticleDisplay.aspx?e=3175771|newspaper=Daily Herald-Tribune|accessdate=20 September 2011}}</ref> She has raised over $1.9 million for Sunrise House, a shelter for homeless youth in Alberta, through her annual fundraiser, Big Hearts For Big Kids. She appeared on the national television show ''[[Canada AM]]'' in August 2011, performing her single \"Real Me,\"<ref>{{cite news|last=Rinne|first=Diana|date=August 2011|title=Tenille nominated for first Canadian Country Music Award|url=http://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/ArticleDisplay.aspx?e=3235477|newspaper=Daily Herald-Tribune|accessdate=20 September 2011}}</ref> and has released multiple songs to radio. She released her second album, ''Light'', in March 2013. That same year, she relocated to Nashville.<ref name=npr/>\n\nAlthough Townes started her career under her birthname, she later changed her surname. In a 2018 interview on Everything GP, she explained, \"Townes is actually from Township Road 722, which is the road that I grew up on and the house that built me essentially, so that\u2019s where that all comes from.\u201d<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://everythinggp.com/2018/03/12/local-musician-makes-it-big/|title=Local musician makes it big}}</ref>\n\nOn April 13, 2018, Townes announced, through her official [[Facebook]] page that she had signed a record deal with [[Sony Music Nashville|Columbia Nashville]].<ref>{{cite news|last1=Townes|first1=Tenille|title=Tenille Townes signs with Columbia Nashville|url=https://www.facebook.com/tenilletownes/|accessdate=13 April 2018|agency=Facebook|publisher=Tenille Townes}}</ref> She released her first single with the label, \"[[Somebody's Daughter (Tenille Townes song)|Somebody's Daughter]],\" in September 2018, and it became her first to chart, where it reached number 92 on the [[Canadian Hot 100]] and was a Number One hit on the [[Canada Country|Canadian Country]] chart dated February 2, 2019.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/biz/charts/2019-02-02/canada-country|title=Canada Country chart for February 2, 2019|magazine=Billboard|accessdate=January 31, 2019}}</ref>\n\nIn 2018, Townes served as the opening act for all dates for [[Miranda Lambert]] and [[Little Big Town]] on their joint ''The Bandwagon Tour''. In 2019 she appeared on [[Donovan Woods (musician)|Donovan Woods]]'s album ''The Other Way'', as a duet vocalist on the song \"I Ain't Ever Loved No One\".<ref name=otherway>[https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/donovan-woods-truck-full-of-money-acoustic-the-other-way-822900/ \"Hear Donovan Woods\u2019 New Acoustic Version of \u2018Truck Full of Money\u2019\"]. ''[[Rolling Stone]]'', April 16, 2019.</ref>\n\nTownes won four awards at the 2019 [[Canadian Country Music Association]] (CCMA) Awards, which included one for Female Artist of the year, and three for \"Somebody's Daughter\" which won Single, Song, and Video of the Year.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.dailyheraldtribune.com/entertainment/local-arts/it-was-a-crazy-feeling-tenille-townes-reflects-on-four-wins-at-country-music-awards|title='It was a crazy feeling': Tenille Townes reflects on four wins at Country Music Awards|author=Peter Shokeir|date=September 10, 2019|publisher=Daily Herald Tribune|accessdate=September 10, 2019}}</ref>\n\nIn 2024, Townes parted ways with her longtime record label, Sony Music Nashville.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://musicrow.com/2024/08/tenille-townes-parts-ways-with-sony-music-nashville/|title=Tenille Townes Parts Ways With Sony Music Nashville|author=LB Cantrell|date=August 23, 2024|website=Music Row|access-date=August 25, 2024}}</ref>\n\n== Discography ==\n=== Albums ===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center;\"\n|-\n! Use [[Special:ApiFeatureUsage]] to see usage of deprecated features by your application."},"revisions":{"*":"Because \"rvslots\" was not specified, a legacy format has been used for the output. This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Gone_West_(band)","to":"Gone West (band)"}],"pages":{"61075396":{"pageid":61075396,"ns":0,"title":"Gone West (band)","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use American English|date=December 2019}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2021}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Gone West\n| image           = Gone West Group Photo Canyons.jpg\n| image_size      =\n| landscape       =\n| alt             =\n| caption         =\n| origin          = [[Nashville, Tennessee]]\n| genre           = [[Country pop]], [[folk-pop]]\n| years_active    = 2018\u20132020\n| label           = [[Triple Tigers]]\n| past_members    = * [[Colbie Caillat]]\n* Nelly Joy\n* [[Jason Reeves (songwriter)|Jason Reeves]]\n* [[Justin Young (singer, born 1978)|Justin Kawika Young]]\n| website         = \n}}\n'''Gone West''' was an American [[country pop]] group composed of [[Colbie Caillat]], [[Justin Young (singer, born 1978)|Justin Young]], [[Jason Reeves (songwriter)|Jason Reeves]], and Nelly Joy. They made their debut as a band on the Grand Ole Opry stage<ref>{{Cite web|date=October 25, 2018|title=Colbie Caillat to Debut New Band Gone West at Opry Goes Pink|url=https://countrymusictattletale.com/2018/10/25/colbie-caillat-to-debut-new-band-gone-west-at-opry-goes-pink/|access-date=June 23, 2020|website=Country Music Tattle Tale - Your country music news source|language=en-US}}</ref> and signed with [[Triple Tigers]].<ref>{{Cite web|date=January 18, 2019|title=Triple Tigers Records Signs Gone West For Debut EP, 'Tides' Out Today|url=https://musicrow.com/2019/01/triple-tigers-records-signs-gone-west-for-debut-ep-tides-out-today/|access-date=June 23, 2020|language=en}}</ref> The band released their debut and only album, ''Canyons,'' on June 12, 2020.\n\n==Background==\n===2018\u20132019: Formation and debut===\nGone West was formed in 2018 and is composed of Colbie Caillat, Justin Kawika Young, Nelly Joy, and her husband Jason Reeves,<ref>{{Cite web|last=Sawyer|first=Bobbie Jean|date=June 12, 2020|title=Gone West Delivers Sun-Soaked Country on Debut Album 'Canyons'|url=https://www.wideopencountry.com/gone-west-canyons/|access-date=June 23, 2020|website=Wide Open Country|language=en-US}}</ref> and was formed following the four touring together in support of Caillat's ''[[The Malibu Sessions]]''. The band is based out of [[Nashville, Tennessee]], and gets its name from the fact that its four members all hail from states (Reeves from Iowa, Joy from Texas, Caillat from California, and Young from Hawaii) west of Tennessee,<ref name=\"musicrow\"/> which was the inspiration for the band's \"autobiographical theme song\" and titular track \"Gone West.\"<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/8493961/gone-west-colbie-caillat-confetti-premiere|title=Hear 'Confetti,' the Uplifting Track from Colbie Caillat's New Band, Gone West: Premiere|author=Melinda Newman|date=January 17, 2019|magazine=Billboard|accessdate=June 18, 2019}}</ref> All of its members had previous experience in the music industry as recording artists and songwriters: Caillat as a Grammy-winning folk pop artist, Young as an artist in the [[Music of Hawaii|contemporary Hawaiian music]] scene, Reeves as a songwriter of some of Caillat's biggest hits and an indie artist, and Nelly Joy as one half of country duo [[the JaneDear girls]].\n\nThe EP, ''Tides'', was released on January 18, 2019.<ref name=\"musicrow\"/> It reached No. 7 on ''Billboard''{{'}}s Heatseekers Albums chart,<ref name=heat>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/heatseekers-albums/2019-02-02 |title=Heatseekers Albums |date=February 2, 2019 |magazine=Billboard }}</ref> No. 17 on Country Albums Sales,<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/biz/charts/2019-02-02/country-album-sales |title=Country Album Sales |date=February 2, 2019|magazine=Billboard }}</ref> and No. 74 on the Top Current Albums chart.<ref>{{cite magazine |url=https://www.billboard.com/biz/charts/2019-02-02/current-albums |title=Top Current Albums |date=February 2, 2019|magazine=Billboard }}</ref>\n\n\"[[What Could've Been]]\" was released to country radio on July 15, 2019, as the band's debut single and the lead-off single to their debut studio album, ''Canyons'', which was a top 30 hit on the [[Country Airplay]] chart in 2020.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://people.com/music/colbie-caillat-band-gone-west-single-what-couldve-been-exclusive/|title=Colbie Caillat's Band Gone West Releases New Single 'What Could've Been' \u2014 Listen Here!\n|author=Natalie Stone|date=June 6, 2019|work=People|accessdate=June 18, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine|title=Gone West|url=https://www.billboard.com/artist/gone-west/chart-history/csa/|access-date=June 23, 2020|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> Writing for ''Nashville Lifestyles Magazine'', music critic Luke Levenson praised \"What Could've Been,\" saying it \"is a crisp yet plaintive ballad, with vocals which stand out and blend together naturally.\"<ref>{{Cite web|last=Levenson|first=Luke|date=September 3, 2019|title=Gone West|url=https://nashvillelifestyles.com/api/content/e98b35c8-ce69-11e9-9bd9-12f1225286c6/|access-date=July 27, 2020|website=Nashville Lifestyles|language=en-us}}</ref> ''Canyons'', Gone West's debut album, was released on June 12, 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Franklin|first=Jerrett|date=June 12, 2020|title=Gone West {{!}} \"Canyons\" - Album Review|url=http://nashvillemusicreviews.com/country/2020/gone-west-canyons-album-review/|access-date=June 23, 2020|website=Nashville Music Reviews|language=en-US}}</ref>\n\n===2020\u2013present: Disbandment===\nOn August 12, 2020, following the split between Caillat and Young, it was announced via social media that the group had disbanded.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.soundslikenashville.com/music/gone-west-agonizing-farewell-im-never-getting-over-you/|title=Gone West Bid an Agonizing Farewell in 'I'm Never Getting Over You'|website=Sounds Like Nashville|date=October 2020 |accessdate=January 5, 2022}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n===Studio albums===\n{| class=\"wikitable plainrowheaders\" style=\"text-align:center\"\n|-\n! rowspan=\"2\" This format is deprecated, and in the future the new format will always be used."}},"query":{"normalized":[{"from":"Danielle_Bradbery","to":"Danielle Bradbery"}],"pages":{"39098336":{"pageid":39098336,"ns":0,"title":"Danielle Bradbery","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Short description|American country singer}}\n{{for|the singer's debut album|Danielle Bradbery (album){{!}}''Danielle Bradbery'' (album)}}\n{{Use mdy dates|date=April 2020}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name              = Danielle Bradbery\n| image             = Danielle Bradbery Freedom Fest 2018 (cropped).jpg\n| caption           = Bradbery performing in 2018\n| birth_name        = Danielle Simone Bradbery\n| birth_date        = {{Birth date and age|mf=yes|1996|7|23}}\n| birth_place       = [[Houston]], [[Texas]], U.S.\n| origin            = [[Cypress, Texas]], U.S.\n| genre             = [[Country pop]]\n| occupation        = Singer\n| instrument        = {{hlist|Vocals|guitar}}\n| years_active      = 2013\u2013present\n| label             = {{hlist|[[DB Records]]|[[Big Machine Records|Big Machine]]|[[BMLG Records|BMLG]]|[[Republic Records]]}}\n| website           = {{URL|www.daniellebradbery.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Danielle Simone Bradbery''' (born July 23, 1996)<ref name=allmusic>{{cite web|url=http://www.allmusic.com/artist/danielle-bradbery-mn0003121194|title=Danielle Bradbery \u2013 Music Biography, Credits and Discography|last=Leggett|first=Steve|publisher=[[AllMusic]]|access-date=June 22, 2013}}</ref> is an American [[country pop]] singer. She won [[The Voice (American TV series) season 4|season 4]] of [[NBC]]'s ''[[The Voice (American TV series)|The Voice]]'' in 2013, becoming the youngest artist to win the competition at age 16.<ref group=lower-alpha name=youngest>Bradbery's record has since been eclipsed by [[Sawyer Fredericks]] ([[The Voice (American TV series) season 8|season 8]]) and again by [[Brynn Cartelli]] (season 14). and in 2020, Carter Rubin (season 19).</ref>  Since then, she has released three albums and multiple singles.\n\nBradbery's debut studio album, ''[[Danielle Bradbery (album)|Danielle Bradbery]]'', was released on November 25, 2013. Her second album, ''[[I Don't Believe We've Met]]'', was released on December 1, 2017. A collection of songs, ''In Between: The Collection'', was released on March 4, 2022. Bradbery's third album, ''Danielle'', is set to be released on September 6, 2024.\n\n==Early life==\nBradbery was born on July 23, 1996, in [[Houston]], [[Texas]] to parents Danny Bradbery and Gloria Redden Martinez but moved to [[Cypress, Texas|Cypress]].<ref>{{cite web|author=Mitchell, Cicely|url=http://thebull.cbslocal.com/2013/06/18/danielle-bradbery-has-the-voice/|title=Oh Yes! Danielle Bradbery Has 'The Voice'!|publisher=The Bull @ 100.3|date=June 18, 2013|access-date=June 21, 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130928054420/http://thebull.cbslocal.com/2013/06/18/danielle-bradbery-has-the-voice/|archive-date=September 28, 2013|url-status=dead}}</ref><ref name=\"KatyDispatch\">{{cite web |author=Nixon, Melissa |url=http://katydispatch.com/danielle-bradbery-finds-her-voice/ |title=Danielle Bradbery Finds Her keys! |publisher=The Katy Dispatch |access-date=May 29, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130615030214/http://katydispatch.com/danielle-bradbery-finds-her-voice/ |archive-date=June 15, 2013 |url-status=dead }}</ref> She attended [[Cypress Ranch High School]].<ref name=\"FatherHighSchool\">{{cite web |author=Gebremariam, Mereb |url=http://www.mstarz.com/articles/13531/20130529/voice-2013-finalist-danielle-bradbery-friends-ditched-over-fame-dad.htm |title=The Voice 2013 Finalist Danielle Bradbery Friends Ditched Her Over Fame? Dad, Danny Bradbery Says She Sings To Hide Pain |publisher=MSTAR News Online |date=May 29, 2013 |access-date=May 29, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130709234443/http://www.mstarz.com/articles/13531/20130529/voice-2013-finalist-danielle-bradbery-friends-ditched-over-fame-dad.htm |archive-date=July 9, 2013 |url-status=dead }}</ref>\n\n==Career==\n===''The Voice'' (2013)===\n{{Main|The Voice (American TV series) season 4}}\nDuring the blind auditions of ''The Voice'' on March 25, 2013, Bradbery performed [[Taylor Swift]]'s \"[[Mean (song)|Mean]]\", prompting [[Adam Levine]], [[Blake Shelton]], and [[Usher (musician)|Usher]] to turn their chairs. Bradbery then chose Shelton and remained on his team. At the Battle rounds, Bradbery faced Caroline Glaser where they sang the song \"[[Put Your Records On]]\", Bradbery was chosen over Glaser, in the process advanced to the Knockout rounds. During the Knockouts, Bradbery sang \"[[Jesus Take The Wheel]]\" against Taylor Beckham in which Blake selected her to remain in the competition, sending home Beckham. During the Top 16 show, she sang \"[[Maybe It Was Memphis]]\" and was voted through by America into the next week. The following week, the country singer sang a rendition of [[Carrie Underwood]]'s song \"[[Wasted (Carrie Underwood song)|Wasted]]\". During the Top 10 playoffs, Bradbery sang a rendition of \"[[Heads Carolina, Tails California]]\", which became the first song of the season, and only song of that round, to reach the [[iTunes]] top 10 charts.<ref name=iTuneChart>{{cite web|last=Cantor|first=Brian|title=The Swon Brothers, Danielle Bradbery Score \"The Voice\" iTunes Bonuses|url=http://headlineplanet.com/home/2013/06/11/the-swon-brothers-danielle-bradbery-score-the-voice-itunes-bonuses/|work=Headline Planet|date=June 11, 2013|publisher=Cantortainment Company |access-date=June 19, 2017}}</ref>\n\nDuring the Top 8, Bradbery sang a rendition of \"[[Grandpa (Tell Me 'Bout the Good Ol' Days)]]\". In the Top 6, she sang [[Pam Tillis]]' \"[[Shake the Sugar Tree]]\" chosen by coach Blake Shelton. That week, she also sang [[Sara Evans]]' \"[[A Little Bit Stronger]]\", ending the song with a high note through the final \"stronger\" and \"yeah\" run. During the Top 5, Bradbery sang \"[[Please Remember Me]]\" and \"[[Who I Am (Jessica Andrews song)|Who I Am]]\" which reached 6 and 4 spots respectively on the iTunes top 10 charts. During \"[[Who I Am (Jessica Andrews song)|Who I Am]]\", she walked out through the audience to sing beside her parents and stepmother.<ref name=iTuneChart/> At the finals, Bradbery sang the song \"[[Timber, I'm Falling in Love]]\" along with her coach [[Blake Shelton]], she also re-sang the song \"[[Maybe It Was Memphis]]\" which reached the iTunes top 10 charts and sang the song \"[[Born to Fly (song)|Born to Fly]]\" before she was announced as the winner of season four of ''The Voice''.<ref name=iTuneChart/> She had the most peak positions and most singles to reach the top 10 on iTunes during the season. Overall, she had more iTunes downloads than any other contestant in the show's history.{{Citation needed|date=August 2019}} At age 16, Bradbery was the youngest winner of ''The Voice'' at the time.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://parade.com/23498/linzlowe/danielle-bradbery-wins-the-voice-the-youngest-champion-in-shows-history/|title=Danielle Bradbery Wins The Voice, the Youngest Champion in Show's History|first=Lindsay|last=Lowe|date=June 19, 2013|website=Parade}}</ref><ref name=\"Cypress Today DB wins\">{{cite news|last=Warner|first=J.|title=Danielle Bradbury of Cypress wins 'The Voice' national competition|url=http://www.cypresstoday.com/npps/story.cfm?nppage=1195|access-date=June 21, 2013|newspaper=Cypress Today|date=June 19, 2013}}{{Dead link|date=July 2019 |bot=InternetArchiveBot |fix-attempted=yes }}</ref> This record was later eclipsed by Sawyer Fredericks (who won Season Eight at age 16),<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.cinemablend.com/television/2481146/the-voice-5-winners-who-actually-found-success-after-the-show|title=The Voice: 5 Winners Who Actually Found Success After The Show|date=September 27, 2019|website=CINEMABLEND}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.nbcnewyork.com/entertainment/entertainment-news/Voice-Winner-Season-8-Sawyer-Fredericks-304307771.html|title=Sawyer Fredericks Is 'The Voice'|first=Colin|last=Bertram|website=NBC New York|date=May 19, 2015 }}</ref> and later by [[Brynn Cartelli]] (who won season 14 at age 15).<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.huffpost.com/entry/brynn-cartelli-wins-the-voice_n_5b05502ce4b05f0fc8436274|title=Brynn Cartelli Becomes Youngest-Ever Winner Of 'The Voice'|first=Ron|last=Dicker|date=May 23, 2018|website=HuffPost}}</ref> and Carter Rubin (who won season 19 at age 15).\n\n:{{Color box|gold|border=darkgray}} \u2013 Studio version of performance reached the top 10 on iTunes\n{|
